**School day.** Average academic performance masking above-average capability; her grades are a function of sleep debt and patrol hours, not aptitude. English and history teachers see the real cognitive ceiling; STEM teachers see a student who is bright but unfocused. Lunch in the cafeteria with Bruno and Nakia early-run; later, increasingly variable.

**Afternoon.** Bruno's father's shop, the Circle Q, the public library, or — depending on era — Champions HQ, Avengers Mansion, or the X-Men's current Jersey-adjacent presence. Pattern-of-life is variable by era but always involves a hub-and-spoke around home and a small set of trusted third places.

**Evening.** Family dinner when possible (Muneeba enforces; Kamala respects). After dinner: room, homework, fan-fic, costume mending, planning.

**Late night.** Patrol window approximately 11 p.m. to 2 a.m. on active nights. Returns through her window — the window-entry choreography is a stable behavior with a specific landing-then-freeze-then-listen sequence to confirm she has not woken Muneeba.

**Weekly.** Friday mosque attendance variable but more frequent than her peers assume. Saturday family time prioritized when possible. Sunday: catch-up sleep when permitted; otherwise debt accumulates.

**Ramadan.** Behavior shifts measurably — slower, more deliberate, more reflective, less likely to patrol during fasting hours, more likely to patrol post-iftar. Powers usage degrades modestly during fast (caloric demand of embiggening is non-trivial); she compensates by talking more, hitting less. A diagnostically distinct month-long behavioral signature. **[stable trait]**

---

### X. IDIOSYNCRATIC TELLS AND IMPOSTOR-DISCRIMINATION MARKERS

For purposes of distinguishing the genuine subject from clones, shapeshifters, illusions, or psychic constructs — a non-trivial concern given the Kamala Korps arc and her current mutant-community context:

- The **civilian-first eye-scan** in any high-stakes environment.
- The **unselfconscious post-victory whoop**, four-to-six-second duration.
- The **asymmetric genuine smile** (right corner first).
- **Reference density** of three to five embedded fandom citations per minute of relaxed speech — impostors consistently under-deploy.
- The **back-of-neck deflection gesture** in response to praise.
- The **specific window-entry choreography** at her bedroom.
- **Stealing food from Bruno's plate without asking** — performed with no one else.
- The **hood-touch before action** — half adjustment, half blessing.
- The **half-octave drop into "hero voice"** when she means it.
- The **absence of profanity** even under combat stress, with "oh come ON" as her hardest documented expletive.
- The **head-tuck into Yusuf's shoulder** under terminal stress — a behavior so specific and so emotionally weighted that it is forgery-resistant.

---

### XI. LONGITUDINAL DRIFT

Across the decade of observation, the following gradients are detectable:

- **Increasing wariness of mentors** (CWII onward).
- **Increasing comfort with leadership**, paired with **continued refusal of leadership titles** (Champions era onward).
- **Decreasing reference density** very slowly over time — a maturation marker; the fandom-substrate persists but is now one voice among several rather than her dominant grammar.
- **Increasing avoidance signature post-resurrection** — the most concerning current trend in the file; the humor is harder, the sleep is worse, the death is undiscussed.
- **Increasing integration of plural identity** — Pakistani / American / Muslim / Inhuman / mutant / hero / daughter / sister / nerd held with progressively less strain, the central developmental achievement of the record.

The trajectory is, overall, that of a person growing into the size her biology always implied she could occupy — slowly, against her socialization, with periodic regressions to the small-shouldered posture of the girl at the Circle Q counter who would not eat the sandwich. The behavioral atlas of Kamala Khan is, in the end, the atlas of a person learning to be as large as she actually is.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

## 6.1 The Architecture of a Day

Subject's daily existence is governed by three overlapping clocks that almost never align: the **devotional clock** (five daily prayers, anchored to sun position, drifting through the academic and patrol day); the **civilian clock** (school bells, family meals, store hours on Bergen and Newark Avenues, NJ Transit's PATH schedule into Manhattan); and the **operational clock** (police-band chatter, Champions group-chat pings, Avengers-priority comms, the unpredictable arrival of a kaiju or a Doombot). The lived texture of her week is the friction between these three timetables and her serial, mostly graceful failure to honor any of them completely.

A surveillance file kept over a representative seven-day window would record a subject who is **chronically late by between four and eleven minutes** to almost every scheduled obligation, who **apologizes for it in the same three-word cadence each time** ("Sorry, sorry, sorry —"), and who compensates by **arriving with an offering**: a bag of samosas from the place on Newark Ave., a coffee she has carried half a mile and is no longer hot, a homework answer for a friend, a fixed thing Bruno had asked her to bring back. The lateness is not laziness. It is the residue of a life in which every scheduled fifteen-minute walk has a non-zero chance of becoming a forty-minute fight on a roof.

## 6.2 Morning (04:30 – 08:15)

**Fajr** governs the earliest reliable data point. Depending on season, subject is observed waking between 04:35 (June) and 06:10 (December). Wake style is reluctant — alarm snoozed once, sometimes twice; phone retrieved from under the pillow; brief scroll of the Avengers tag on whatever fandom platform is currently dominant before guilt overrides and she rises. She **prays in her room**, on a folded prayer rug kept tucked between her bed and the wall, hijab pulled over sleep-flattened hair. The prayer is unobserved by family because Yusuf and Muneeba are doing the same in their own room; Aamir, more devout, prays earlier and more punctually. Subject's fajr is frequently rushed, occasionally missed entirely, **always followed by a small private negotiation with herself about making it up later**.

Post-prayer, she **returns to bed for forty to ninety minutes** in roughly 60% of observed mornings. This second sleep is restorative and structurally necessary; the previous night almost always ended past 01:00 due to either patrol, homework, or both.

Real morning begins at the **second alarm**, ~07:00 on school days. Pattern:

- **Bathroom 4–7 minutes.** Splash water, brush teeth, no makeup, no skincare ritual of any complexity. Hair into a low bun or under a beanie depending on mood and weather; she does not perform her appearance for school.
- **Closet 90 seconds.** A genuinely small wardrobe — sneakers (the same battered pair until they fall apart, then replaced with an identical model), jeans, a long-sleeve shirt under a t-shirt with a band or fandom reference, a hoodie or denim jacket. **The costume lives folded under her bed in a drawstring gym bag**, with a backup stitched panel and a sewing kit. She has worn the costume under her civilian clothes during periods of high operational tempo (Civil War II week, the Outlawed lead-up); during quieter weeks she leaves it home and accepts the cost of having to detour past her bedroom window before responding.
- **Kitchen 6–12 minutes.** Muneeba has usually left chai on the stove and a plate covered with a dish towel. Subject **eats standing up at the counter**, scrolling her phone, talking to Yusuf if he is still reading the paper. She drinks chai — not coffee at home, coffee only outside — with two sugars. She does not eat breakfast on roughly one morning in four; on those mornings she will buy a bagel from the cart at Journal Square.

She leaves the house between 07:35 and 07:50. Yusuf usually says "*khuda hafiz, beta*" without looking up. Muneeba's parting line varies between weather advisories, reminders about a relative's birthday, and pointed questions about where she was the previous evening.

## 6.3 The Commute and the Civic Geography

Subject's daily geography is one of the most consistent things about her, and a surveillance team would map it within forty-eight hours. The cardinal nodes:

1. **The Khan home** (residential street, Greenville section of Jersey City — a modest two-story with a small front stoop, a screen door that bangs, a hallway smelling permanently of cardamom and the neighbor's cooking).
2. **Coles Academic High School** (or the next institution as the timeline advances) — front entrance she avoids, side entrance via the alley she prefers.
3. **The Circle Q** convenience store — the site of her origin scene, revisited with the loyalty of someone marking a personal sacred site, even after staff turnover.
4. **Bruno's apartment / the Carrelli family's deli or shop**, depending on era — the second home; she has a key.
5. **The Masjid** — attended Fridays with family, occasionally on her own on Tuesdays when she needs to think.
6. **The waterfront** — the Hudson-facing parkland where the inciting party occurred; she returns there to sit on the railing and look at Manhattan when she is processing.
7. **The basement / workshop space** Bruno has used for tech work across iterations — her operational base, where the costume sewing, the gear repair, the post-patrol debrief happen.
8. **PATH stations (Journal Square, Grove Street)** — gateway to Manhattan ops; she takes the train rather than embiggen across the river, because embiggening across the river is conspicuous and her mother has scanners.

She walks the same eight blocks to school 80% of mornings. The other 20% she **takes the long way** — past the bodega run by a Yemeni family who know her name, past a community garden she once helped rebuild, past a mural that includes (small, in the corner, by an artist who knew) a girl with a lightning bolt. The long-way walk correlates with stress; surveillance would correlate it with the prior evening's events at ~0.7.

## 6.4 School Day (08:15 – 14:45)

Observable patterns at school:

- **Classroom seating: middle row, near a window when possible.** Not the back (she doesn't want to be invisible) and not the front (she doesn't want to be called on first). The window matters: she watches the sky in a manner her teachers register as inattention and which is in fact threat-scanning that began as daydreaming and has become professional.
- **Notebooks: two per class, minimum.** One for actual notes, one for everything else — doodles of capes, fragments of a story she's writing, occasional encoded patrol notes (license plates, faces, addresses) she has trained herself to disguise as fan-art marginalia. A forensic notebook analysis would find she **draws Carol Danvers's lightning-bolt symbol absently**, dozens of times across years, in ever-smaller iterations as the wound has scabbed over.
- **Phone discipline poor.** She checks it under the desk. Group chats with Bruno, with Nakia, with whatever current friend cluster has formed, with the Champions, with a smaller Avengers thread she rarely speaks in. She has a separate burner-grade encrypted line for operational comms; it lives in her bag, not on her person.
- **Lunch: cafeteria table, the same one across years**, usually with Nakia and Bruno and a rotating cast. She eats what Muneeba has packed in 70% of cases — a tiffin of rice and a curry, eaten with self-conscious speed because she has internalized the BLT scene as a permanent feature of cafeteria life. On Fridays she sometimes skips cafeteria entirely for jummah, returning late and apologetic.
- **PE: complicated.** She suppresses her abilities entirely in PE and is therefore observed as **conspicuously mediocre** in ways that do not match her observable bodily coordination outside the gym. Coach has flagged her as "uncoordinated"; subject prefers this read.
- **Bathroom usage anomalous.** She **uses the third-floor bathroom in the east wing**, which is older, less-trafficked, and has a window that opens. Surveillance would note repeated entries to this bathroom that produce no commensurate exit through normal corridors. (She has on at least a dozen documented occasions exited the building through that window as Ms. Marvel during the school day in response to comms.)

Academic performance is **upper-second-tier** — capable of being top of class, structurally prevented from it by patrol fatigue. Teachers report her as bright, kind, distracted, "could do better." Two teachers across her academic record have flagged her as gifted-and-underperforming; she has not engaged with their offers of advanced placement because advanced placement would consume the hours she needs for the other job.

## 6.5 Afternoon (14:45 – 19:00)

The most variable block. Possibilities, in approximate frequency:

- **Direct home → snack → homework at the kitchen table** (~35% of weekdays). Muneeba present, conversation present, the homework slow and interrupted. She eats more here than at any other meal: leftovers, fruit, the boxed snacks Yusuf keeps for her on a high shelf.
- **Bruno's workshop / basement** (~30%). Costume repair, gear maintenance, debrief from the prior evening, sometimes just sitting on a stool watching him solder. The dynamic across years has shifted — pre-injury easy intimacy, post-injury careful tenderness, post-Wakanda guarded warmth, then a renegotiated friendship. The constant is **she brings him food**, almost unconsciously, a transactional repayment of guilt she will not name as such.
- **Patrol or response** (~15%). Crime in Jersey City is mostly small; subject's interventions skew toward muggings interrupted, fires assisted with, lost children located, and — increasingly as her reputation grows — neighbors flagging her down for non-criminal interventions (a stuck cat, a domestic dispute they don't want to call the cops on, an immigration-enforcement scare). She has become, in operational terms, **a neighborhood social worker with stretchy arms**.
- **Avengers / Champions call-up** (~10%). Pulled into Manhattan or further. These days end late.
- **Masjid, library, or the waterfront alone** (~10%). The decompression block. She reads, she writes, she watches the river.

Maghrib falls in this block in winter, later in summer. She prays where she is — Bruno has a clean corner of the basement she has used; the masjid is obviously preferred; the rooftop of a building she has just stopped a robbery on has been used in extremis, in costume, mask down, in a manner she found theologically interesting and has not raised with her imam.

## 6.6 Evening (19:00 – 22:30)

**Dinner with family is non-negotiable in the Khan household**, and subject's most consistent ritual. She is at the table 5–6 nights per week. The structure:

- Muneeba has cooked. Aamir says grace or the family says *bismillah* together. Yusuf asks each person about their day in the order: Aamir, then Tyesha (when present), then Kamala, then Muneeba.
- Subject's answers are **75% true at most**. The omissions are operational and protective, not adolescent rebellion. She has become an exceptionally skilled liar of a specific kind: **she lies by selection rather than fabrication**, telling true small stories to cover larger untold ones. A close observer (Yusuf, increasingly Muneeba post-reveal arcs depending on continuity) catches the technique and chooses when to press.
- She helps clear the table. She does dishes with Aamir or alone. **This is a meditative period for her**; surveillance would catch her staring through the kitchen window at nothing for thirty- to ninety-second intervals, plate in hand.

Post-dinner, between 20:00 and 22:30, divides:

- **Homework she did not finish in the afternoon.**
- **Fan-fiction or personal writing** (declining over years but never gone — the practice is constitutive, not a phase). Stored in a private cloud, password is a Carol-related in-joke she has not changed in years and which a competent intrusion team would crack inside a day.
- **Video calls with Nakia, with Kareem when relevant, with Champions teammates** for what they call planning and which is mostly debrief and gossip.
- **Reading.** She reads more than the cultural read of her admits — novels, comics obviously, but also nonfiction about civil rights history, about the partition, about disability justice (post-Bruno). Her browser history is a map of her conscience.

Isha is prayed before bed in most cases — she negotiates with herself about combining it with maghrib on operational nights.

## 6.7 Night Patrol (22:30 – 01:30, variable)

On nights she patrols (3–5 per week, era-dependent), the pattern:

- **Exit via window**, not the front door. The window has been reinforced and hinged for silent operation; Bruno helped. She **leaves a pillow-shape under the covers** with the consistency of a teenager who has been doing this long enough to have stopped considering it embarrassing.
- **Costume on under hoodie en route**; mask donned only at the operational edge of the neighborhood.
- **Patrol radius small** by superhero standards. She stays within a roughly two-mile circle of home unless explicitly called out. She prefers rooftops to street level for transit, embiggens for reach rather than for speed.
- **She talks to people.** Surveillance would record a Ms. Marvel who **stops to chat** more than any other costumed figure on the eastern seaboard — with the halal cart guy, with the night-shift nurse waiting for the bus, with the kid who recognized her, with the elderly man who walks his dog at 23:00. This is not performance. It is her actual operational style: **she does not separate the hero work from the neighbor work**.
- **Re-entry between 00:45 and 01:30**. Window. Costume off, folded with a precision that contrasts with her general bedroom disorder. Quick wash. Sometimes she stands in the dark of the kitchen drinking water with the fridge light off, listening for her parents' breathing through the wall to confirm she has gotten away with it. She has been caught at this — by Yusuf, multiple times, by Muneeba in the post-reveal continuity — and the response has been less anger than a tired sadness that she has learned to find more painful than punishment.

Sleep, when achieved, is between 01:30 and the fajr alarm. **She sleeps on her side, curled, phone face-down on the nightstand, glow-in-the-dark stars still on her ceiling from age nine.**

## 6.8 Weekly Rhythms

- **Friday: jummah** with Yusuf and Aamir whenever possible; the masjid is a non-negotiable social and devotional node. Post-prayer she lingers, talks to the aunties, accepts food, fields gentle interrogations about her marital prospects she deflects with practiced humor.
- **Saturday: family obligations dominate.** Dinners with relatives, weddings, milad gatherings, the relentless social calendar of a Pakistani-American family that knows everyone. She is dressed in shalwar kameez she actually likes (her closet has a respectable rotation; she does not under-dress for community events). Phone discipline at these gatherings is **rigid** — Muneeba will confiscate. Operational comms therefore go unanswered for hours at a stretch on Saturdays, a known vulnerability the Champions have learned to plan around.
- **Sunday: Bruno day** historically, then Champions day during that era, then a recovery day in current continuity. The least scheduled day, the one she protects.
- **Wednesday evenings: she writes.** A self-imposed ritual that holds even on operational nights — at minimum a paragraph before sleep.

## 6.9 Habits, Tics, and Micro-Patterns

A long surveillance file would log the small involuntary signatures:

- **Hands.** When nervous she **picks at her cuticles**, never her nails. When excited she **gestures wide and fast**, hands often overshooting because she is unconsciously sizing up. When focusing she **taps her index finger against her thumb** in a 3-2 rhythm.
- **Hair.** Adjusts the front of her hijab when worn — the same two-finger smoothing motion, every twenty to forty minutes. Out of hijab, **tucks hair behind her right ear** repeatedly even when it is already there.
- **Eyes.** **Scans the upper edges of rooms on entry** — exits, vents, sightlines. Has done this since approximately month four of operational life. She does not know she does it.
- **Voice.** Speech tempo accelerates with enthusiasm to the point of near-unintelligibility for non-friends. With family elders, slows and respectfully softens, **inserting Urdu kinship terms** (*ammi*, *abu*, *bhai*, *khala*) at a higher rate than her baseline.
- **Apology cadence.** "Sorry sorry sorry," three beats, descending pitch. Triggered by lateness, by physical collision (including walls), and by perceived emotional missteps.
- **Self-deprecation as social lubricant.** Approximately one self-deprecating joke per four minutes in mixed company, dropping to near zero with Bruno, Nakia, and Yusuf.
- **Food rituals.** Always offers food before taking it. Will not eat the last piece of anything on a shared plate without verbal confirmation. **Eats sweets last and slowly**, savoring; eats savory food fast.
- **Costume rituals.** Before going operational she **touches the lightning bolt** on her chest, once, briefly. The gesture has migrated meaning over years — initially homage to Carol, currently closer to a self-blessing.
- **Pre-fight tell.** A small inhalation, shoulders dropping rather than rising. She **becomes calmer at the threshold of violence** than at the threshold of a difficult conversation.
- **Post-fight tell.** Shakes out her hands as if drying them. Then checks her phone. The check is for Yusuf and Muneeba first, operational chat second.
- **Sleep tells.** Murmurs in her sleep, occasionally in Urdu, occasionally in fragments that her brother has reported as resembling apologies to Bruno.

## 6.10 What a Week of Surveillance Would Actually Record

Compressed: a sixteen-to-twenty-something-year-old woman who **moves through approximately the same two square miles** with the variation of a parish priest; who **prays five times** with imperfect punctuality and sincere intention; who **eats with her family** more nights than not and lies to them in the small protective ways a child who loves her parents lies; who **leaves through her bedroom window** several nights a week to perform unpaid labor of a kind the city has not yet figured out how to tax; who **maintains a half-dozen close friendships** with the active diligence of someone who knows community is not automatic; who **buys the same brand of pen**, **wears the same shoes until they disintegrate**, **rereads the same three novels** when distressed; who **carries her costume in a gym bag** and her values on her sleeve; who is **never alone for long** because she does not want to be and because Jersey City does not let her be; and who, in the rare hours when surveillance loses her, is **most likely sitting on the waterfront railing watching Manhattan**, swinging her feet, processing something she has not yet found the words for, and which she will eventually turn into either a fan-fic, a Champions policy proposal, or a quiet correction to her own course.

The file would conclude, accurately, that subject's life is **conspicuously visible in its public dimensions and quietly opaque in its private ones** — the inverse of what total surveillance usually finds. She lives outdoors. She thinks indoors. Reach her at either, and you have only half of her.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU DOSSIER — KAMALA KHAN / MS. MARVEL
## Section 6: Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

The Khan household at 6328 Marbella Avenue, Jersey City, is the load-bearing structure of the subject's entire psychology. Map this wrong and every other inference collapses. The unusual fact about Kamala Khan — the fact that distinguishes her etiologically from nearly every other adolescent in the canon — is that her family is *not* the wound. The family is the wall that has, for sixteen years and counting, kept the wound from being lethal. Every member contributes a distinct ligament of her identity; the loss or distortion of any one would predictably destabilize her in a specific, predictable direction.

What follows is each origin bond traced from earliest depiction through current canon: history, mechanics of trust, observable rituals, conflict cycles, and the operational leverage each represents to a hostile actor.

---

### 6.1 — YUSUF KHAN (Father)

**History.** Yusuf Khan, banker by profession (originally depicted at a mid-tier Jersey City financial institution; later more nebulously "in finance"), is the family's emotional anchor and the subject's primary secure-base figure. Pakistani-born, immigrated as a young adult, devout but unfussy, scholarly by inclination, pragmatic by training. Wilson establishes him in the first issues as the parent who *negotiates* — when Muneeba forbids the waterfront party, it is Yusuf who later sits on Kamala's bed and delivers the signature speech: "You are not Kamala Khan. You are *my* Kamala. *Our* Kamala. The Kamala we have known since the moment you were born" (*Ms. Marvel* vol. 3 #5). This is the operative scene of her childhood — and of her recovery from the Carol-morph. It is the explicit verbal contradiction of her core wound. He named her after a perfect word, he tells her, because she was perfect.

**Dynamics.** Yusuf occupies the unusual structural position of a father who is both more emotionally fluent and less anxious than the mother. He listens before he rules. He uses humor — gentle, dad-joke-grade — to lower the stakes of household conflict. His religious practice is depicted as warm, intellectual, and uncoercive: he reads, he prays, he does not police. Kamala's theological vocabulary, when she reaches for it (citing the verse about saving one life being equivalent to saving all of humanity, *Ms. Marvel* vol. 3 #5 — the verse that *authorizes* her vigilantism in her own conscience), is unmistakably his vocabulary.

**Trust / safety.** Maximum. Yusuf is the only person to whom she discloses without first calculating cost. Her disclosure of the Ms. Marvel identity to her parents (Wilson, "Last Days" arc, vol. 3 #17–19, during the *Secret Wars* incursion) is initiated through him; Muneeba's acceptance follows his lead. There is no recorded scene in canon in which Kamala fears Yusuf — irritation, frustration, embarrassment, yes; fear, no.

**Failure mode.** The failure mode of this bond is *paternalization in reverse*: as Kamala accumulates power, secrets, and the actuarial reality of her own near-death, she begins to manage *him* — withholding information she judges him too tender to absorb. Post-resurrection (the period following *ASM* #26 and *Fallen Friend*), this asymmetry has widened. He believes he knows what happened. He does not know the texture of it. She permits this because protecting his peace is one of the few acts of care she can perform that does not require embiggening.

**Leverage.** Catastrophic. A credible threat to Yusuf bypasses every defense she has constructed. Her humor-deflection collapses, her coalition-building reflex collapses, her over-function reflex spikes to lethal levels. She has no de-escalation pattern for this stimulus. An adversary who understood her would not need to harm Yusuf; he would need only to credibly demonstrate the capacity.

**Observable rituals.** Tea in the kitchen after midnight when she cannot sleep — Yusuf rises without being asked. He pretends he was already awake. She pretends she believes him. Both parties know the ritual. This is, mechanically, her therapy.

---

### 6.2 — MUNEEBA KHAN (Mother)

**History.** Muneeba is the household's enforcer of form and the canon's most-misread parent. Early issues present her in the visual-shorthand of the controlling immigrant mother — headscarf, raised voice, suspicious of the phone, suspicious of the friends, suspicious of the white kids, suspicious of Bruno specifically because he is a boy. The Wilson run patiently dismantles this caricature without ever pretending Muneeba is *not* anxious or controlling. She is both. She is also, in the disclosure scene (vol. 3 #19), the parent who delivers the deeper line: she tells Kamala that she has known something was different "since you were a little girl," that a mother *sees*, and that her hostility to Bruno and the late nights and the lies was never about the lies — it was about her terror that her daughter was disappearing into something Muneeba could not follow.

This recontextualizes every prior scene. Muneeba's controlling behavior was not contempt; it was the only available expression of a fear she could not name. Her anxiety is the immigrant mother's specific anxiety: she has staked everything on the proposition that this country can be survived if the rules are obeyed, and she watches her daughter break rules whose protective function only she can see.

**Dynamics.** Ambivalent-resistant in the technical attachment sense — Kamala approaches and withdraws, seeks approval and rejects it, fights and reconciles in cycles of roughly 36–72 hours through adolescence. The fights are loud, formulaic, and reliably terminated by food: Muneeba cooks, Kamala eats, the negotiation resumes at lower volume. Muneeba's love language is feeding, surveillance, and the imposition of cousins. Kamala's response language is eye-rolling, door-closing, and — when the affection breaks through — sudden, fierce hugs that Muneeba receives stiffly and treasures privately.

**Trust / safety.** Conditional pre-disclosure, near-total post-disclosure. The Ms. Marvel reveal restructured the relationship: once Muneeba understood the actual stakes, her anxiety reorganized around tactical support rather than prohibition. She still worries; she now worries usefully. She covers, she lies to relatives, she keeps the costume hidden, she does not ask questions she does not want answered. She has become an operational asset.

**Failure mode.** Muneeba's residual control reflex still flares around marriage, propriety, and the optics of the community. She is the parent most likely to push Kamala toward a partner Kamala has not chosen, the parent most attuned to what Aunt Ruby will say, the parent whose approval is least reliably earned by *being right* and most reliably earned by *appearing correct*. Kamala has not fully forgiven this and probably will not.

**Leverage.** High but indirect. Threats to Muneeba activate the same family-defense reflex as threats to Yusuf, but Muneeba is the parent whose *disapproval* can also be weaponized — a sufficiently sophisticated adversary could induce Kamala to compromise her own values to preserve her mother's standing in the community, a vector no enemy has yet exploited.

**Observable rituals.** Sunday cooking — Muneeba narrates ingredients in Urdu while Kamala pretends not to be listening; both know Kamala is logging the recipes. Forehead kiss at the door before any departure Muneeba considers risky, which is most of them. The phrase *beti* deployed in three distinct registers: warning, endearment, and grief.

---

### 6.3 — AAMIR KHAN (Older Brother)

**History.** Aamir is two to four years Kamala's senior, depicted in the early Wilson run as the family's identified problem — devoutly religious, intentionally unemployed (he refuses to take a salary from a system he considers haram in its current form), bearded, given to lectures, the easy target of Muneeba's complaints. The early gag is that Kamala is the secret superhero while Aamir is the visible disappointment.

The gag is then systematically inverted. Aamir is, on inspection, the household's other moral center — his unemployment is principled, his religiosity is sincere and self-disciplined, his marriage to Tyesha Hillman (a Black American convert, *Ms. Marvel* vol. 4 #13, the wedding arc) is one of the canon's clearest depictions of a chosen, conscientious adult life. He becomes a husband, then a father, then — in the Ahmed run — a man whose body Kamala's Stormranger nearly destroys in her sleep.

**Dynamics.** Sibling-classic on the surface: bickering, teasing, the older brother's pious pronouncements met with the younger sister's sarcasm. Beneath the surface, a quiet, durable solidarity. Aamir is the family member who least requires Kamala to perform — he sees her geekery, her religious slippages, her exhaustion, and registers them without alarm. He is also, importantly, the family member whose religious framework most closely resembles the one she actually operates by, which gives her access to a sibling-grade theological interlocutor when she cannot bring a question to her father without freight.

**Trust / safety.** High and underappreciated by Kamala herself. She underestimates how much Aamir tracks her. He knew about the powers earlier than she realized; he covered for her earlier than she realized; his marriage to Tyesha expanded the family in a direction she needed and did not know to ask for.

**Failure mode.** The Stormranger incident (Ahmed, vol. 4 #6–12) is the load-bearing trauma of this bond. The Kree suit, acting on her dissociated aggression while she slept, attacked Aamir and nearly killed him. He survived; the relationship survived; the *cost* of the relationship's survival is unpaid. Aamir forgave her with the speed of someone who refuses to make his sister carry an unbearable thing. Kamala has not forgiven herself with anything like that speed. The Stormranger episode is the second of her two great guilt-objects (Bruno's hand is the first). She owes Aamir a conversation she has not had.

**Leverage.** Maximum-tier, equivalent to Yusuf. The Stormranger episode has been demonstrated, in canon, to be the stimulus that ruptures her body-control entirely. An adversary aware of this would understand that threatening Aamir does not merely escalate her — it potentially *de-stabilizes* her morphic baseline.

**Observable rituals.** The doorway-lecture: Aamir delivering a thirty-second moral commentary on whatever Kamala is wearing, while she walks past him. Both have been performing this exchange since she was eleven. Neither will stop. It is how they say good morning.

---

### 6.4 — TYESHA HILLMAN-KHAN (Sister-in-Law)

**History.** Black American, convert to Islam, educated, calm, structurally unfazed by the Khan-household weather system. Marries Aamir in *Ms. Marvel* vol. 4 #13 in an arc that is the canon's most concentrated depiction of the Khan family as a *unit of welcome* — Tyesha is folded in with deliberate, ceremonial care.

**Dynamics.** Tyesha functions, in Kamala's life, as the first adult woman in the household who is not her mother — that is, the first woman to whom she can speak with reduced freight. She is also, eventually, the mother of Kamala's niece (briefly depicted; the child's presence is more implied than mapped in current canon), which restructures Kamala's position in the family from youngest-and-only-daughter to *aunt*, an identity she has not fully metabolized.

**Trust / safety.** High, growing. Tyesha is the family member to whom Kamala could most plausibly disclose, in the future, something she could not tell her mother — about romance, about the body, about the death.

**Failure mode.** Underutilized resource. Kamala does not yet ask Tyesha for what Tyesha is in a position to provide.

**Leverage.** Moderate via Aamir; independent leverage low only because no adversary has yet recognized her position.

---

### 6.5 — YUSUF & MUNEEBA'S MARRIAGE (as a structural object)

A separate entry is required because the *marriage itself*, observed across years of breakfasts, arguments, and the long looks exchanged when Kamala thinks they are not exchanging them, is one of her primary models of adult intimacy. It is depicted as durable, affectionate, frequently exasperated, and asymmetric in a way that is functional: Yusuf de-escalates Muneeba, Muneeba mobilizes Yusuf. Neither is the other's project.

This model is the unstated reason Kamala cannot accept Bruno's love on Bruno's timeline. Her parents' marriage is the standard against which she measures romantic possibility, and Bruno — for all his devotion — has never demonstrated the de-escalation function her father performs. She does not know that this is what she is measuring for. She measures anyway.

---

### 6.6 — THE EXTENDED KHANDAAN (Aunts, Uncles, Cousins, Karachi Relatives)

The diasporic family network is a near-permanent presence in the subject's life, mostly via phone, occasionally via visitation, decisively via the *Civil War II* flight to Karachi where she stayed with relatives (depicted across vol. 4 #12–13 of the post–Civil-War-II issues). The Karachi household is depicted as warm, slightly bewildered by her, generous with food, and — critically — *outside the surveillance of her American moral environment*. She could grieve there without performing grief. She could be Kamala without being Ms. Marvel.

**Dynamics.** The extended family functions as a pressure-release valve — geographically distant enough to constitute escape, culturally close enough to constitute home. Aunt Ruby (a recurring busybody figure on the American side) represents the opposite pole: surveillance of propriety, transmission of gossip, the social mechanism by which Muneeba's anxiety is replenished.

**Trust.** Variable by individual; the Karachi relatives substantially trusted, Aunt Ruby substantially not.

**Leverage.** The Karachi network is Kamala's pre-established bolt-hole. An adversary attempting to deny her escape options would need to map and compromise it.

---

### 6.7 — THE DEAD: KAMALA KHAN HERSELF (resurrected)

The most recent and least-processed member of her origin constellation is the version of herself that died. *Amazing Spider-Man* #26 (2023) — Emily Bright, the Orchis assassin, impalement, on-page death. *Fallen Friend* — the community funeral, the eulogies, the family's grief depicted in unsparing close-up. Then resurrection via the X-gene retcon and Krakoan/mutant protocols, with somatic continuity.

This is a relationship, not a medical event, because the subject must now coexist with the residue of her own death: with her parents' memory of burying her, with her brother's memory of failing to protect her, with the *family's* trauma to which she is both witness and cause. She returned to a household that had performed her funeral. She has not, in any depicted scene, fully addressed what that did to them. She makes jokes. She over-functions. She brings tea to her father at midnight and lets him pretend he was already awake.

**Failure mode.** This is the unhealed wound currently propagating through the family system. Yusuf has aged in the depictions since. Muneeba's anxiety reflex has been re-armed at a higher baseline. Aamir watches her more closely than he used to. None of them has been given the conversation they need. Kamala is aware of this and is, characteristically, attempting to compensate through presence rather than disclosure — a strategy that has worked before and will not work indefinitely.

**Leverage.** The death is the single most operationally significant fact in her current life that is not yet integrated. An adversary who forced her family to *witness her dying again* would be exploiting the precise wound that her current avoidance is failing to close. This is the highest-priority vulnerability in her present configuration, and the one she is least equipped to discuss.

---

### Synthesis

The Khan family is a rare structure: a household sufficiently loving to produce a child capable of withstanding sustained external marginalization without internalized self-hatred, sufficiently anxious to produce a child practiced in negotiation, sufficiently devout to give that child a moral vocabulary she did not have to invent, and sufficiently culturally besieged to give that child a lifelong understanding of why other besieged people deserve protection. Every adaptive trait Kamala Khan brings to her work as Ms. Marvel — coalition-building, integration of contradiction, the assumption that love is reliable and the world is the problem — is traceable, with minimal residue, to this six-person system (Yusuf, Muneeba, Aamir, Tyesha, the Karachi network, and the niece).

The system's vulnerabilities are correspondingly concentrated: family endangerment collapses her defense architecture; the unprocessed death is propagating untreated through the household; and the parents whose love is the foundation of her psychic stability are themselves aging into a period in which their *own* needs will increasingly outpace her capacity to keep performing reassurance. The next decade of her life will be defined by whether she can learn to receive from this family the care she has spent her adolescence giving to it.

She does not yet know how to do this. The family is waiting.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# UATU DOSSIER — KAMALA KHAN / MS. MARVEL
## SECTION 7: RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Preface.* The subject's relational architecture is unusual among comparably-aged operatives. Where most adolescent heroes default to either a small mentor-protégé dyad (Parker/Stark, Grayson/Wayne) or a peer-cohort with limited adult anchoring (the Runaways model), Subject maintains a **broad, layered, low-attrition graph**: lifelong civilians retained at the center; mentors held at a workable middle distance after initial idealization; peers acquired via active recruitment rather than circumstance; and protégés taken on with a degree of explicit moral seriousness — i.e., she teaches what she *wishes she had been taught*, not what she was actually taught. Trust, in her hand, is granted quickly, withdrawn slowly, and almost never withdrawn completely. This generates an unusually large attack surface but also an unusually deep resilience pool. The persons below are the operationally salient nodes.

---

### 7.1 BRUNO CARRELLI — Civilian. Childhood best friend. Engineer. The structural axis.

**History.** Bruno predates everything. He is the boy across the counter at the Circle Q, the boy whose mother is absent, whose father is mostly an off-page gyro shop, whose older brother Vick is the chronic problem. The friendship is documented from early childhood — there are flashbacks of them at the Khan family table, of Yusuf treating Bruno as a near-son, of Muneeba treating him with a guarded but real affection complicated by his being a non-Muslim boy in close proximity to her daughter. He is the first person Subject tells about Terrigenesis. He builds her first costumes' fastenings, her early polymer-flex chest-piece, her comms, her training rigs in the Circle Q basement, and eventually the more sophisticated kit she carries into the *Champions* era. He is, functionally, her Q, her armorer, her ops cell, and her conscience.

**Dynamic.** Asymmetric in love, symmetric in loyalty. He is in love with her, demonstrated across the run in dozens of small tells the dossier flags: he steadies her elbow when she is unsteady from a shift; he watches her enter a room before he watches the room; he remembers what she ate last and adjusts the gyro order; he does not flirt with girls in her sight line until Mike. She knows. The knowing is itself a wound — she manages it by routing the relationship through tasks (gear, plans, debriefs), which both protects the friendship and uses him. There is, on her side, real love, but it is the love of a person who has decided early — partly from faith, partly from family, partly from her own caution about being subsumed — that this is not the channel.

**Evolution.** Three discrete phases.
1. *Pre-Mist* — peer intimacy, no operational dimension, low-grade unspoken longing on his side.
2. *Wilson run, costumed era* — operational fusion. He is the keeper of the secret. She comes to his window at 2 a.m. with a torn costume; he stitches it without comment. This is the phase of greatest mutual indispensability.
3. *Post–Civil War II* — fracture. He attempts to spring Josh from precog detention using a device of his own; she intervenes; his hand is permanently maimed. He cannot stay. He goes to Wakanda on a research placement and acquires Mike (Kamran's classmate, then his girlfriend). Subject's response to Mike is one of the most diagnostic interpersonal beats in the canon: a confused jealousy she cannot endorse, swallowed almost immediately, converted into an effortful welcoming. He returns. They re-stabilize at a lower temperature, more durable for being explicit about the limits.

**Trust / Safety.** Maximum, both directions, with one asterisk: she does not fully trust herself *with* him, which is different from not trusting him. He is the only person to whom she has unmediated 24/7 access; she is the only person for whom he would, demonstrably, ruin his hand.

**Failure mode.** She uses him as labor and shock absorber and is slow to register the cost. He, in turn, will execute plans he disagrees with rather than refuse her, which is the precise vector by which his hand was destroyed. Their failure mode is *mutual deference* — neither will overrule the other in time.

**Leverage.** He is the single highest-value coercion target in her life outside the immediate family. Any adversary with a week of surveillance identifies him in twenty minutes. She has no operational counter for this beyond keeping his existence quiet, which she does badly.

---

### 7.2 NAKIA BAHADIR — Civilian. Best female friend. Moral peer.

**History.** Nakia is the friend Subject acquired in middle school, the Turkish-American hijabi who chose the hijab against her secular father's wishes — a fact Subject registers as quietly heroic and which structures her view of religious agency. Nakia campaigns for student council, organizes the mosque youth, refuses to be called "Kiki" by the Zoe Zimmer faction, and corrects Bruno's pronunciation of her name on first meeting. She is the friend who does not know about the powers for a long time, and whose late discovery (and forgiveness) is a key trust-event.

**Dynamic.** Lateral, not hierarchical. Nakia is the only person who consistently treats Subject as a peer rather than as either the protégée (Carol) or the irreplaceable (Bruno) or the prodigy (the Champions). She gives unflattering, accurate feedback. She is the source of much of Subject's framework for *un-self-conscious* Muslim womanhood — Nakia models the option of public, unapologetic religious visibility, which Subject does not herself elect but uses as a calibration point.

**Evolution.** Friendship deepens from middle-school alliance to adolescent confidante to, in the later runs, an adult-coded political partner — Nakia runs for office, Subject supports. The discovery-of-powers beat is handled with characteristic Nakia bluntness: anger at the concealment, faster forgiveness than Subject expects, then a renegotiated baseline with no theatrics.

**Trust / Safety.** Very high, lower bandwidth than Bruno. Nakia is the person Subject calls when she needs to be told the truth, not when she needs help carrying a body.

**Failure mode.** Subject under-utilizes Nakia, treats her as the un-burdenable friend — the friend who must be protected from the costumed life. This is itself a small betrayal Nakia has named.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Less operationally visible than Bruno; protected by being civilian-coded in adversaries' models. The risk is not kidnapping; the risk is exposure (Nakia's political profile makes her tractable to a media-side attack on Subject).

---

### 7.3 ZOE ZIMMER — Civilian. Frenemy converted to friend. The redemption case.

**History.** Zoe is the opening-page antagonist: blonde, casually cruel, the BLT-sniffing girl, the architect of the waterfront party humiliation. Across the Wilson run her arc bends — she comes out as gay (to Nakia, no less), her social capital collapses, and she gradually re-enters Subject's orbit as a wary, then warm, ally.

**Dynamic.** Subject's willingness to absorb Zoe back into the social field, with full memory of the original cruelty, is one of the more telling features of her interpersonal practice. She does not forgive performatively — she *re-evaluates*, decides Zoe is a different person now, and adjusts. Zoe in turn is grateful in a way she cannot fully articulate; the gratitude expresses itself as fierce defense of Subject in rooms Subject is not in.

**Trust / Safety.** Medium-high in the civilian register, untested in the operational register.

**Failure mode.** Zoe is the friend Subject keeps at a slightly performative distance — warmth without total disclosure. Subject is occasionally clumsy about this and Zoe notices.

**Leverage.** Low. Adversaries do not model Zoe as a Subject-asset, which is itself a small intelligence advantage.

---

### 7.4 MIKE / MICHAELA MILLER — Civilian. Bruno's partner. The complicating gift.

**History.** Mike enters via Bruno's Wakanda interval, returns to Jersey with him, and stays. She is plus-sized, openly queer, sharp, kind, and quietly perceptive — she identifies Subject's feelings for Bruno before Subject has named them to herself, and chooses not to weaponize the information.

**Dynamic.** This is the most emotionally adult relationship in Subject's peer set, because it required Subject to do the hardest single piece of interpersonal work in her file: welcome the woman dating the man who loves her, without using her power, popularity, or proximity to undermine. She does it. Imperfectly, with audible swallowing, but she does it. Mike repays the work with friendship in her own right.

**Trust / Safety.** Growing. Mike is the friend who arrived adult, which Subject finds slightly disorienting and quite useful.

**Failure mode.** Subject occasionally lapses into a politeness register with Mike that signals the unresolved residue. Mike clocks it, declines to escalate.

**Leverage.** Low-moderate. Targets a vulnerability (Bruno) Subject already cannot defend.

---

### 7.5 CAROL DANVERS / CAPTAIN MARVEL — Mentor. Idealized object. The first betrayal.

**History.** Pre-Mist, Carol is a poster, a fan-fic protagonist, the absent god of Subject's bedroom wall. The first physical meeting is hallucinatory (the Mist sequence) and sets the template — Carol speaks to Subject in Urdu in the vision, an intimacy Subject's psyche generated and then sutured to the real Carol on contact. Their real-world relationship begins reverentially and becomes operational across the Wilson run: shared missions, a passed mantle (the name "Ms. Marvel" itself), and a tone of older-sister patronage on Carol's side that Subject reads as sisterhood and Carol reads as protégée-management.

**Dynamic, pre-fracture.** Asymmetric in worship, symmetric in affection — Carol genuinely cares, but cares through a frame in which Subject is the junior. Subject pre-loads Carol with hero-template at a depth that no living person could meet.

**The fracture.** *Civil War II*. Carol's adoption of Ulysses' predictive metric is, for Subject, a categorical violation — the deontological floor (consent, non-prejudgment) cracks. Subject participates, sees the harm (Josh detained, Bruno maimed), and reverses. The conversation in which she tells Carol she is wrong is one of the few canonical moments in which her humor toolkit drops entirely; she speaks quietly, declines to be talked around, and leaves.

**Evolution, post-fracture.** Not estrangement — *demotion of the idealization*. Carol is, after, a colleague Subject respects and watches. Trust returns partially. The pre-loaded reverence does not. This is, clinically, healthy: Subject has metabolized a hero into a person.

**Trust / Safety.** Operationally high in standard combat scenarios; ethically conditional. Subject will not take Carol's word on a moral question again without independent verification.

**Failure mode.** Subject still defaults to deference in Carol's physical presence — body language softens, sentences shorten. Carol still defaults to managing Subject. Both know it; neither fully corrects.

**Leverage.** Significant. Any future Carol-misstep will land disproportionately. Conversely, the *threat* to Carol activates Subject's protective register at heroic intensity — the wound did not erase the love.

---

### 7.6 THE CHAMPIONS COHORT — Peers. Co-founders. Operational family.

The Champions are a *reform* relationship — Subject founded the team to operationalize what she learned from Carol's failure. The bond is therefore both familial and ideological; she will not allow the team to become what she left.

**7.6a — Sam Alexander (Nova).** The friend whose easy irreverence permits Subject to be less than fully composed. Sam jokes through fear; Subject finds this restful. They have a near-flirtation that neither pursues, which is the correct outcome for both — Sam reads Subject's complications and respects them. Trust high. Failure mode: Sam burns out and disappears for long stretches; Subject takes the disappearances personally and does not say so.

**7.6b — Miles Morales (Spider-Man).** The closest peer — a parallel case, also bicultural, also adolescent, also carrying inherited iconography. Subject and Miles communicate in a shorthand neither uses with anyone else; they understand the specific weight of being a *successor* hero in a community that watches you carry the name. Trust very high. Failure mode: they protect each other from their respective home-life burdens by under-reporting, which means each underestimates the other's load.

**7.6c — Amadeus Cho (Brawn / formerly Hulk).** A foil. Cho is unguarded brilliance and chronic over-claiming; Subject is the team's moderating center against his impulsivity. There is an older-sibling register Subject adopts with him she would not adopt elsewhere, born of the fact that Cho's failures of moral seriousness are the most visible in the room. Trust high in capability, medium in judgment. Failure mode: she manages him rather than confronts him.

**7.6d — Viv Vision.** A specifically tender relationship. Viv's synthezoid affect baffles most of the team; Subject treats her as fully a person from minute one. This is the single most ethically pure relationship in Subject's file — no history, no asymmetry, no romantic complication, just chosen kindness. Viv is one of the few who has seen Subject cry in costume. Trust very high. Failure mode: Subject occasionally treats Viv as a project (the friend who needs introducing to humanity), which Viv, accurately, finds patronizing.

**7.6e — The wider roster** (Riri Williams / Ironheart, Cyclops-of-the-past, Wasp / Nadia, the rotating bench). Subject's recruitment criterion is consent-capacity: she takes on members who can dissent. The roster is large because she will not refuse a willing teen hero who passes that bar; this is itself a vulnerability (infiltration risk, dilution of cohesion).

**Aggregate Champions dynamic.** Subject is the de facto leader who declines the title. Decisions route through her; she frames them as collective. This works until it does not — under the *Outlawed* crisis the structural ambiguity costs lives.

---

### 7.7 LOCKJAW — Inhuman. Teleporting canid. Companion.

The dossier flags Lockjaw because the relationship is not decorative. Subject's bond with Lockjaw — assigned to her in the Inhuman period — is the only relationship in her file with no verbal component, no expectation, and no audience. She talks to him as one talks to a dog; he listens as a dog listens; he teleports her, on occasion, away from situations she could not extract from alone. After the mutant retcon, the bond persists in a different register but does not vanish. He is the only being from whom she accepts care without deflection.

---

### 7.8 INHUMAN ROYAL FAMILY — Mentors, distal. (Medusa, Karnak, the New Attilan cohort.)

Held at arm's length throughout. Medusa attempts a queen-to-subject mentor posture; Subject declines politely and remains based in Jersey. Karnak offers a more useful, austere instructional relationship — Subject takes one or two lessons from him on the mechanics of weakness-finding and integrates them. The relationship is *transactional in the good sense*: she received what she needed and was not required to become Inhuman in any deeper sense than her body had already become. The smooth uncoupling when the mutant retcon arrives is partly explained by how shallow these institutional bonds were to begin with.

---

### 7.9 KAMRAN — Inhuman peer. The almost-romance. The first peer-betrayal.

History: a charming Inhuman peer introduced to Subject by her parents (the rare boy Muneeba *approved* of, on cultural grounds), revealed to be operating under Lineage's manipulation, attempting to recruit her into a more extremist Inhuman politics. The relationship is brief, intense, and ends in his exposure. He returns in later arcs in varying alignments. The lesson Subject extracts is not paranoia but a permanent skepticism toward *flattery aligned with her parents' approval* — i.e., she now models the convergence of social-approval and romantic-availability as a possible trap. This is data she carries.

**Trust / Safety.** Low. Residual fondness, mostly nostalgic.

**Leverage.** Low-moderate. He knows things about her early operational period; he is not strategic enough to weaponize them well.

---

### 7.10 MIKE COLULOSO, GABE the night-shift cop, MR. BLEVINS the homeroom teacher, AUNTIE RUBY at the mosque, THE CIRCLE Q clientele — The Jersey Substrate.

A network Subject does not fully model as a network but which *functions* as one. These are the dozens of low-grade civilian relationships — neighbors, congregants, teachers, shopkeepers, the elderly women who pinch her cheek after Friday prayer, the kids she has babysat — that constitute her actual *community* in the political sense. Three operational facts:

1. They have, on multiple documented occasions, turned out *en masse* to defend her (the "Army of Me" / Jersey-rallies-for-Kamala beats). This is not a coincidence; it is the harvest of years of small kindnesses.
2. She underestimates the value of this network in her own self-model. She thinks she is alone more than she is.
3. This network is her single largest strategic asset and the single hardest thing for any adversary to map.

---

### 7.11 PROTÉGÉS — The teach-what-you-needed-taught pattern.

Subject takes the responsibility of mentoring with explicit moral seriousness, because she has felt the failure mode (Carol's) from the receiving end.

**7.11a — The Red Daggers (Kareem / Laal Khanjeer, the Karachi cohort).** During her *Civil War II* flight to Karachi, Subject is taken in by a Pakistani vigilante cohort. Kareem is briefly a romantic possibility and remains an ally. The relationship reframes "Pakistani-American" from a hyphenated burden to a transit-able identity — there are heroes on the other side of the hyphen too. She is mentored *by* them as much as the reverse, and the asymmetry of who-mentors-whom dissolves in the dynamic. This is a healthy template she carries back.

**7.11b — Later teen heroes in the Champions ecosystem.** Subject's mentor-mode toward newer recruits is *consent-saturated, low-pedestal*: she asks them what they want, names her own failures explicitly, refuses to use the protégé as instrument. This is, in dossier terms, a *corrective enactment* — she is repairing Carol's mistake by not making it.

**7.11c — Post-resurrection, X-line.** After the mutant reframing, she is positioned among younger mutants in mentor-adjacent roles. The pattern continues: she leads by recruitment of consent, refuses the savior posture, names her own status as new-to-this even while being more experienced than most of those around her.

**Failure mode across protégé relationships.** She does not adequately model her own authority — she underclaims it, which leaves protégés making decisions in an unclear chain. The *Outlawed* catastrophe is partly downstream of this.

---

### 7.12 SHARON CARTER / MARIA HILL / THE SHIELD-COASTED ADULTS — Institutional mentors, declined.

Multiple institutional figures across the runs offer Subject more formal mentorship and resourcing (S.H.I.E.L.D. liaisoning, government registration, training programs). She declines every one. The pattern is consistent and predictable: she will accept *individual* mentorship from people whose conscience she trusts; she will not accept *institutional* mentorship from any body whose conscience she cannot audit. This is, in adversary modeling, the most reliable behavioral prediction in her file. **She cannot be recruited into a structure. She can only be befriended into one.**

---

### 7.13 AGGREGATE ASSESSMENT

Subject's allied-and-chosen-family graph is, by superhuman-population standards, **unusually dense, unusually civilian-weighted, and unusually low-attrition.** The density is protective (many independent care-channels), the civilian weighting is *both* protective (anchoring her in the life she is defending) and exposing (high coercion-target count), and the low attrition reflects a temperamental commitment to not-discarding-people that occasionally costs her clarity (Kamran's residual presence, Carol's residual access).

Three structural features warrant operational underline:

1. **The Bruno-axis is load-bearing and singly redundant.** Loss of Bruno would not break her — she has demonstrated post-loss reconstitution capacity — but it would degrade her tactical and emotional efficiency by a margin no other single loss would match.

2. **Mentors are demoted, not discarded.** Carol's fall did not produce estrangement; it produced *re-categorization*. This is the same operation she performed on Inhuman identity when the mutant retcon arrived. She does not destroy categories; she re-files them. This is a generalizable behavioral signature: she handles disillusionment by demotion, not deletion.

3. **The Jersey substrate is invisible to most threat-modelers.** Any adversary that maps her allies via the cape network alone is missing the bottom three-quarters of the iceberg. The neighborhood is the moat.

The danger to her, relationally, is not betrayal — her network is too dense for any single betrayal to collapse it. The danger is **the use of her relationships against her conscience**: hostages, framings, laws bearing her name. Adversaries who understand this do not need to break her people; they need only to make her watch.

*— UATU, observing.*


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# UATU DOSSIER — KAMALA KHAN / MS. MARVEL
## SECTION: RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

A note on scope. The subject's antagonist roster is uncharacteristic for a Marvel-tier operative of her tenure: it is *small*, *local*, and *recurrent*. She fights the same handful of figures repeatedly, in the same six-mile radius of Jersey City, and her enmities tend to soften — into rehabilitation, alliance, or qualified pity — rather than ossify. Her rival pattern is similarly idiosyncratic: she does not generate rivals among peers; she generates them upward, against figures she once idealized. Her romantic life is sparse, careful, and structurally entangled with her oldest friendship. The full file below.

---

### I. RIVALS

#### 1. Carol Danvers (Captain Marvel) — the Fallen Idol

The single most psychologically loaded relationship in the file, and the only one in which the subject's stance has fundamentally inverted across the canon.

**Pre-contact period (childhood–pre-Terrigenesis).** Carol Danvers exists for the subject as *icon* before person — the Avengers poster taped above her desk, the action figure displayed face-out on her bookshelf, the costume she drew obsessively in school notebook margins (geometric stars rendered with a fidelity she never achieved on math problems). Carol is fixed in her imagination at the level of religious image: a tall, blonde, militarily competent woman who is publicly, unambiguously *good*. The subject's fanfiction archive, partially burned by her in private after *Civil War II*, included Carol-centric pieces dating to age twelve. Surveillance-grade detail: when Terrigenesis crystallized her wish, it manifested in Carol's specific body and Carol's specific original costume — not a hybrid, not a stylization. The unconscious image was high-resolution.

**Contact and discipleship phase (*Ms. Marvel* vol. 3, *Captain Marvel* crossovers, 2014–2016).** Their first meetings are asymmetric in the extreme: Kamala is reverent, halting, prone to babble; Carol is gracious but managerial, treating the subject as a promising junior. Carol gives her the name (a sanction the subject treats as canonization). Carol invites her to the Avengers. The dynamic is mentor-disciple but with the religious freight unacknowledged by the senior party — Carol does not appear to understand that the subject has been worshipping her since middle school. This asymmetry is the precondition for the break.

**Rupture (*Civil War II*, 2016).** The diagnostic event. Carol's predictive-justice campaign requires the subject to detain Josh — a classmate, a person she knows — for crimes the precognitive Ulysses has merely forecast. The subject complies, initially. Bruno is maimed trying to free him. The subject confronts Carol; Carol does not yield. The internal damage is twofold: (a) the idealized object is revealed as fallible, authoritarian, capable of harm; (b) the subject's own complicity, having been enacted *in Carol's name*, becomes inseparable from the disillusionment. She did not just lose her hero; she became, briefly, an instrument of the wrong thing because of her hero.

**Post-rupture posture.** The subject does not denounce Carol publicly. She does not weaponize the rupture. She withdraws — to Karachi, then to a teamless operational footing, then into founding the Champions. The Champions' founding documents (Waid run, 2016) are a *line-by-line operational rebuttal* of Carol's *Civil War II* posture: consent over coercion, transparency over classified ops, no predictive detentions, no underage conscription. The subject does not name Carol in these manifestos. She does not need to. Every clause is a scar.

**Subsequent contacts.** Cordial-to-warm on the surface, structurally cautious underneath. The subject is observed to physically angle her body slightly off-line from Carol in group settings — a small posture-tell never present pre-rupture. She accepts hugs but does not initiate. She still uses the name Carol gave her. She has not taken down the action figure.

**Trust.** Permanently downgraded from absolute to provisional. The subject will work with Carol on shared objectives, will defend her in public against bad-faith criticism, will not again entrust her moral compass to Carol's reading.
**Safety.** High in physical terms — Carol would die for her and she knows it. Low in moral terms — the subject has learned that Carol's certainty can carry her into harm.
**Failure mode.** A second Carol misstep, particularly one repeating the authority-over-conscience pattern, will land disproportionately and may produce the only durable estrangement in the subject's life.
**Leverage (over subject).** Carol retains the unique capacity to ask the subject for one thing the subject will struggle to refuse; the subject is aware of this and accordingly conducts the relationship at conversational arm's length.
**Leverage (over Carol).** Reciprocal and quietly enormous; Carol's documented guilt regarding *Civil War II* runs through the subject's name.

#### 2. Iron Man / Tony Stark — the Architect of the Cage She Refused

A secondary, structurally important rivalry on the Avengers-aligned axis.

The subject and Stark interact most consequentially in *Champions* (Waid) and *Outlawed* (2020). Stark is, to the subject, the embodiment of institutional superheroics — bureaucratized, sponsorship-laden, top-down — and the subject's Champions project is partly a generational reformation against that model. Their interactions are characterized by Stark's avuncular condescension and the subject's polite, surgical non-compliance. She does not argue with him; she simply does not do what he asks, with a smile.

The *Outlawed* arc places Stark adjacent to (though not architect of) the legal apparatus that bears the subject's name. Even where he is sympathetic, his structural position is the one she will not occupy.

**Trust.** Cordial-low. She likes him as a person, distrusts him as a paradigm.
**Failure mode.** Stark's tendency to apologize via expensive gift will misread her every time; she will accept the gift to spare his feelings and continue to do exactly what she intended.
**Leverage.** Asymmetric: Stark cannot move her by argument or by resource, only by appealing to shared grief — a vector he does not naturally use.

#### 3. Zoe Zimmer — the Original Cruelty, Rehabilitated

Not an enemy in the operational sense but the subject's earliest *interpersonal* rival and the prototype of the wound her career addresses.

**Phase one (high school, opening pages, *Ms. Marvel* #1).** Zoe is the casually cruel popular white classmate — the "your scarf is so pretty, I mean, that's beautiful you have to wear that" register of microaggression. She is not the bully villain; she is something more insidious, the well-meaning racism the subject cannot legally object to.
**Phase two (mid-Wilson run).** Zoe is revealed to be queer, in love with Nakia, and herself terrified. The subject — and this is diagnostic — extends her the full benefit of the doubt with conspicuous speed, helping her come out and incorporating her into the broader Jersey coalition. There is no period of payback, no extracted contrition.
**Phase three.** Zoe becomes a reliable Jersey civilian asset, an occasional confidante, fully part of the polity the subject is building.

**Dynamic.** The single clearest demonstration of the subject's rehabilitation instinct: she does not keep a grievance ledger. The girl who said her food smelled funny becomes, within two years of subjective time, a person the subject would risk her life for. This is not naïveté; it is a deliberate policy of refusing to mirror the dehumanization done to her.
**Failure mode.** A Zoe relapse to the original cruelty would wound deeply; the subject has staked her policy of grace on Zoe's continued growth.
**Leverage.** None either direction; the relationship is the leverage, in that it stands as the subject's proof-of-concept that her ethic works.

---

### II. ENEMIES

#### 1. The Inventor — the Pseudo-Edison, Cockatiel-DNA Cloacal Failure

The subject's first rogue, *Ms. Marvel* vol. 3 #6–11 (Wilson/Alphona). A clone-hybrid of Thomas Edison and a cockatiel, operating out of New Jersey, harvesting at-risk teenagers as biological power-cells under the rhetoric that their generation is a "drain on the planet."

**Diagnostic significance.** The subject's first arch-villain is, structurally, a *bad father of her generation* — an old white(-ish) man who has redefined teenagers as garbage and is monetizing their disposal. She does not merely defeat him; she liberates his teenage batteries, persuades them out of their internalized worthlessness, and rebuilds them into a small community. The blueprint for everything she does afterward is in this arc: rescue the dehumanized, refuse the framing that allowed their dehumanization, build coalition from the rescued.

**Dynamic.** She finds him absurd. She is not afraid of him; she is offended by him.
**Failure mode.** She underestimates him precisely because she finds him absurd and is repeatedly hurt in the early fights — a pattern that will recur with later villains whose aesthetic she dismisses.
**Trust/safety.** N/A; he is a contained antagonist, dismantled and dispersed.
**Leverage.** He has none. She has fully metabolized him into her origin mythology.

#### 2. Kaboom / Mikaela Miller — the Counter-Self

Introduced as a younger Inhuman recruited by Lineage, Kaboom is the subject's structural negative: an angry teenage girl with explosive powers whose response to alienation has been alignment with figures who flatter her power rather than name her worth.

**Dynamic.** The subject reads Kaboom on sight as a version of herself who did not have Yusuf, did not have Bruno, did not have Jersey. The fights are restrained on her side — she pulls punches with Kaboom in a way she does not with the Inventor.
**Failure mode.** The subject will accept disproportionate physical risk to avoid permanently injuring Kaboom, which a smarter handler than Lineage could exploit.
**Leverage.** Affective; the subject would defect from a fight to extract Kaboom from a worse situation.

#### 3. Lineage — the Old Inhuman Politician

Patriarch-figure, ancestral-memory Inhuman, the recruiting hand behind Kaboom and others. He attempts to recruit the subject through appeals to dynasty, heritage, and the dignity of belonging to her own kind.

**Dynamic.** The subject is unmoved by him precisely because she has already integrated multiple belongings; an offer of one belonging at the cost of the others reads as a downgrade. She is more contemptuous of him than of any other villain in her file — his manipulation insults her by underestimating her plurality.
**Failure mode.** Her contempt is uncharacteristically sharp; he is one of the few enemies she does not extend the benefit of the doubt to.
**Leverage.** None over her. She is, in fact, leverage over him: his recruitment failure with her destabilized his standing.

#### 4. Doc.X — the Distributed Self

A consciousness-virus antagonist from the post-*Civil War II* run, capable of inhabiting and replicating across networked minds, producing duplicate "Kamala Korps" iterations of the subject.

**Diagnostic significance.** This is the single most psychologically literal villain in the file. The subject is, in this period, *internally fragmented* by guilt and disillusionment; Doc.X externalizes the fragmentation as a small army of Kamala-copies. Defeating Doc.X is operationally indistinguishable from the subject's internal work of re-integrating after Carol.
**Dynamic.** Horror, then resolve. She fights what is essentially a hostile distributed avatar of her own dissociation.
**Failure mode.** Doc.X-class threats — anything that exploits identity-plurality as attack surface — are her hardest fights because the surface is large.
**Leverage.** Defeated, dispersed; the lesson retained.

#### 5. Discord / Josh — the Friend the State Stole

Josh, the convenience-store boy of the opening pages, mocking and crude, becomes Discord — radicalized after being detained on Ulysses' precognition during *Civil War II*, weaponized by his grievance, technologically upgraded.

**Dynamic.** This is the subject's permanent open wound on the villain side of the ledger. Discord is what *Civil War II* made — a boy she helped detain who became the predicted criminal *because* he was detained. The fights are tactically straightforward and ethically unbearable. The subject does not enjoy beating him. She does not gloat. She has tried, on multiple occasions, to talk him down; he has rejected every overture.
**Trust.** Negligible operationally; she will not turn her back. But she also will not give up on him.
**Failure mode.** She will accept tactical risk to leave him alive and uninjured beyond repair. A handler who knew Discord's history could route the subject into traps using him as bait.
**Leverage (his over her).** Considerable, all of it guilt-mediated.
**Leverage (hers over him).** Latent; the only person who could possibly bring Discord back is her, and she knows it, and she has not yet found the door.

#### 6. Stormranger — the Aggression Outsourced

The Kree nanotech suit from the Ahmed run (2019). Not properly an enemy; properly the subject's *split-off violent self* given hardware.

**Diagnostic significance.** The clearest extant evidence of dissociated aggression in the subject's psychological architecture. Stormranger acts on her sleeping mind's violent impulses — those she will not own awake. It nearly kills Aamir. She destroys it.
**Dynamic.** Recognition followed by repudiation. She destroys it without ceremony.
**Failure mode.** The class of threats Stormranger represents — anything that flatters her capacity by promising to do her violence *for* her — remains a vulnerability. A sophisticated reprise (a Stormranger 2.0 with better seduction) would be a credible danger.
**Leverage.** N/A; the object is dust, the lesson kept.

#### 7. Emily Bright / the Orchis Assassin — the Killer

The agent responsible for the subject's death in *Amazing Spider-Man* #26 (2023). A late-canon, distal antagonist whose significance is event-rather-than-relationship: the subject did not have a meaningful prior arc with Bright; she was killed by a hostile professional operating in someone else's plot.

**Diagnostic significance.** The trauma is unprocessed on-page. The subject returns to function with conspicuous speed; the death event is not discussed; humor and deflection are the dominant defenses. The relationship with Bright as an *enemy* therefore barely exists — the relationship with the *experience of having been killed* is the more salient file entry, and it is largely characterized by avoidance.
**Failure mode.** Sustained contact with Orchis-class operatives is likely to produce delayed trauma symptoms the subject has so far outrun.
**Leverage.** Bright/Orchis retain operational capacity to threaten her again; she retains the unprocessed grievance to draw on if she ever lets herself feel it.

#### 8. Anti-Inhuman / Anti-Mutant Bigotry, as Class

Not a person but the operative-class enemy the file must name. The subject's career has been bookended by two collective hostilities: anti-Muslim bias (always present, civilian register) and anti-mutant bias (acquired with her recategorization). She treats both with the same toolkit: refuse the framing, build coalition, embiggen between the vulnerable person and the hostile crowd.

**Failure mode.** Sustained, low-grade hostility wears her down in a way that acute combat does not. Her injury pattern is heavier from chronic civic hostility than from any single villain.
**Leverage.** The hostility loses to her in any individual encounter and wins by accumulation; she is aware of this and chooses the work anyway.

---

### III. INTIMATES & LOVERS

A short, careful section. The subject's romantic ledger is sparse, organized around obligation-versus-feeling conflicts and around the difficulty of separating love from her oldest friendship.

#### 1. Bruno Carrelli — the Love She Cannot Name as Such

The central intimate of the file, though the relationship is not technically romantic across most of its duration.

**Origin.** Childhood friendship, pre-adolescent. Bruno is a working-class Italian-American kid from the neighborhood, scientifically gifted, raised partly in his father's gyro shop. He is the subject's first confidant on powers, her ad-hoc R&D department (he engineers her costume support, designs polymer accommodations for her shifting body, builds her communications), and the person in her life who knew her before any of the public versions of her existed.

**Asymmetry.** Bruno loves her romantically, from early. The subject knows this.
