Her own feelings are real, deep, ambiguous, and obstructed: by family expectation (a non-Muslim boyfriend would be a familial crisis Yusuf could weather and Muneeba could not), by her own observance, and — diagnostically — by her unwillingness to risk the friendship that is her most stabilizing tie. She chooses, repeatedly, the friendship over the romance, knowing she is hurting him by doing so.

**Crisis (*Civil War II*).** Bruno is maimed — left hand crippled, partially numbed — trying to free Josh. The subject's recklessness contributes to the injury. This is the most enduring guilt-load in her file. Bruno departs for Wakanda for rehabilitation and study, in part to put physical distance between himself and the romantic situation as much as to recover.

**Subsequent posture.** Cordial, intermittently re-engaged, never fully resolved. He has had other partners. She has had other prospects. Neither has stopped being the other's emergency contact in the way that matters.

**Trust.** Maximum, with the qualification that they both know they hurt each other.
**Safety.** Physical maximum. Emotional, asymmetric — he is safer with her than she with him, because he has done the work of knowing her, while she has avoided the work of knowing what she wants.
**Failure mode.** A serious romantic threat to Bruno (his marriage to someone else, say) would force a feeling-event she has not consented to have. A serious physical threat to Bruno bypasses every de-escalation circuit in her toolkit; observers should expect disproportionate response.
**Leverage (his over her).** Total and unwielded — he has never used it.
**Leverage (hers over him).** Total and used only inadvertently — every time she chooses friendship over romance she exercises it.

#### 2. Kamran — the Beautiful Wrong One

Introduced (Wilson run, *Ms. Marvel* vol. 4) as the parent-approved suitor: handsome, charming, Pakistani-American, Muslim, the boy Muneeba would have engineered if she could.

**Phase one.** The subject's first reciprocated romantic-adjacent feeling. Real attraction, real warmth, brief flowering. The contrast with Bruno is structurally important: Kamran is *allowed*, and the subject experiences the relief of a permitted desire.
**Phase two.** Kamran turns out to be a NuHuman recruited by Lineage's faction, attempting to bring her into a coercive Inhuman politics. The romance is partially instrumental from his side, partially genuine, fully compromised.
**Phase three.** Hostility. He becomes an antagonist, with intermittent attempts at re-seduction by appeals to shared identity. She refuses, repeatedly, with hardening clarity.

**Diagnostic significance.** Her first romantic disillusionment is structurally homologous to her Carol disillusionment: an idealized figure who turns out to be using her as instrument for an agenda she rejects. The wound is smaller (less pre-loading) but the pattern is the same, which suggests a vulnerability — the subject is *liable to* relationships in which she is being recruited rather than known. Bruno's significance, by contrast, is that he is the only major intimate who has never been trying to recruit her into anything.

**Trust.** Destroyed and not rebuilt.
**Failure mode.** A sophisticated future seduction along Kamran-vector — handsome, culturally fluent, ideologically aligned, ulteriorly motivated — would still have non-trivial purchase on her unless she catches the recruitment signature early.
**Leverage.** Negligible for him now; she has updated.

#### 3. Red Dagger / Kareem — the Parallel Hero

A Pakistani vigilante introduced during the subject's Karachi-flight arc (post–*Civil War II*) and recurring thereafter. Their dynamic is the only properly *romantic-and-equal* relationship in the file: he is a hero in his own right, operationally peer, culturally legible to her in ways no American boy can be, and unencumbered by the friendship-debt of Bruno.

**Phase one (Karachi).** Solidarity, attraction, the relief of being a hero in a place where she does not also have to be an explainer of herself. Kareem sees her whole.
**Phase two (Jersey City visits).** He visits the States; they pursue a tentative relationship; geography, schedule, and her unresolved Bruno-knot prevent it from becoming central.
**Phase three.** Ongoing low-amplitude warmth; they remain in each other's lives without having converted the relationship into a defining tie.

**Diagnostic significance.** Kareem is what the subject's romantic life *could be* if she ever resolved the Bruno question. The fact that she has not converted him into a primary partner — despite his being approximately optimal on paper — is itself evidence that the Bruno tie occupies the slot.

**Trust.** High.
**Safety.** High.
**Failure mode.** The relationship is structurally vulnerable to her decision-deferral; he is patient but not infinitely so, and a Kareem departure would be a non-trivial loss she has not priced.
**Leverage.** Mutual and gently exercised; neither has weaponized the affection.

#### 4. Romantic Pattern, Synthesized

Three data points, three lessons:
- Bruno: she will not destabilize a load-bearing friendship by clarifying her own desire.
- Kamran: she is susceptible to permitted desire and must learn to screen for instrumental motive within it.
- Kareem: she can have a healthy, equal partnership when geography and the Bruno-slot make it possible; she has not made it possible.

The integrating fact: the subject organizes intimacy the way she organizes citizenship — plurally, in tension, refusing to collapse into a single allegiance. This is psychologically continuous with everything else in her file. Whether it is sustainable into adulthood is the open question her current canon has not yet answered.

---

### IV. CROSS-CUTTING OBSERVATIONS

**On her rival/enemy pattern.** She does not generate horizontal rivals — peers her age in the superhero community do not become her antagonists; they become her teammates. Her rivals are exclusively upward (Carol, Stark) and her enemies are exclusively figures who have already failed somebody (the Inventor failing the young, Lineage failing his community, Kam


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: KAMALA KHAN / MS. MARVEL
## Section 6 — Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

### 6.1 The Master Mechanism: Polymorphism

Subject's primary ability is best classified as **voluntary somatic polymorphism**: conscious redistribution of her own cellular mass and morphology under will, with the body itself serving as the substrate. Originally classified as Inhuman, later retconned as a latent X-gene activated by Terrigenesis (per *Fallen Friend*, 2023, and subsequent X-Men line), the underlying mechanism is functionally the same regardless of taxonomic label. Whatever the genome of record, the **expressed phenotype** is a body that can be re-sculpted by intent.

The implication, which is the analytic key to everything that follows, is that her power is **not external** (no projected energy, no field, no tool, no construct outside her skin). Her superpower is *her body, refusing to be fixed*. Every limit, every signature, every metaphor returns to this.

The constituent capacities subordinate to polymorphism are:

1. **Macro-scaling ("embiggening").** Voluntary expansion of overall mass and volume, or of discrete body parts, scaling from her baseline ~5'4" up to documented states approaching building-height in extremis. Most operational use is selective: the Giant Fist, the Giant Foot, the Giant Hand-as-Shield. Full-body giant form is rare, taxing, and often misjudged.
2. **Micro-scaling ("shrinking").** Inverse capacity; she can compress to insect-scale, demonstrated in early Wilson issues for infiltration and escape. Used less frequently than embiggening — a behavioral preference discussed in §6.6.
3. **Elongation.** The most-used and most-versatile subset. Limbs (especially arms and legs) extend on the order of tens of meters reliably, further with effort. This is the "Mr. Fantastic" subset of her toolkit and serves both offense (long reach strikes), mobility (grappling, swinging, vaulting), and rescue (catching falling civilians at distance).
4. **Shape-mimicry / face-shifting.** Limited but real. She can approximate other human forms — established at origin via the inadvertent Carol Danvers transformation, retained as a low-use capacity. She rarely uses it. The reason is psychological, not mechanical: every shape-mimic act is a re-enactment of the original wound (§6.6).
5. **Accelerated healing, morph-dependent.** Injuries close as she returns to baseline; the polymorphic reset *is* the healing mechanism. This couples regeneration directly to identity-collapse: she heals by becoming most-herself.
6. **Tactile-volumetric awareness.** Implied across the canon: she has fine proprioceptive control over distributed mass, can punch with calibrated force at scale, can catch a child without crushing them in a giant hand. This is a learned skill, not a baseline (early issues show her constantly misjudging her own size).

### 6.2 Range, Scale, and Hard Limits

**Mass conservation versus mass apparent.** The canon is inconsistent on whether her growth conserves mass (denser-when-small, less-dense-when-large) or violates it (genuine creation/dissipation of mass). Observed behavior favors a *hybrid*: small applications appear mass-conservative (her giant fist hits with momentum consistent with her usual body, hence the surprise of opponents who expect a wrecking-ball impact); large-scale full-body giant form behaves as if she has acquired genuine mass and inertia, which she struggles to control. The behavioral consequence: **she is more dangerous than she looks at small scale and more vulnerable than she looks at large scale.**

**Energetic cost.** Polymorphism is metabolically expensive. Signatures of overuse: tremor, nausea, blackout, involuntary reversion to baseline, hunger spikes (she is repeatedly depicted ravenous after heavy power use — the canonical post-fight gyro is not a gag, it is a refueling event). She has no internal warning system finely enough tuned; she discovers her limits by exceeding them. This is the **principal injury vector** across her career.

**Injury forces baseline.** Sufficient damage collapses any held form. Tactically: a sufficiently determined opponent can negate her transformation entirely by hurting her enough to make her body revert. This is a structural vulnerability — she cannot fight wounded *and* shaped.

**Concentration dependence.** Holding a non-baseline form is an act of sustained will. Sleep disrupts it (Stormranger arc); unconsciousness ends it; severe emotional dysregulation degrades it. In early issues she could not maintain a face in front of her parents without lapsing.

**Costume substrate.** Her clothing does not natively shift with her body. The first costume is purpose-built (repurposed dishdasha, hand-sewn) of an unstable-molecules analog that grows with her. Civilian clothing tears when she embiggens — a recurring quiet visual gag and an operational constraint that has forced her to costume-up before action more often than other heroes do.

**No projection, no flight, no energy attack.** Her toolkit is entirely body-mediated. She has no ranged offense except to elongate a limb into the target. She does not fly; mobility at altitude requires improvisation (elongated arm as grappling hook, giant leap). She does not blast. This is operationally significant: against ranged opponents in open terrain she is at a profound disadvantage and must close, evade, or improvise cover.

**Mimicry limits.** Shape-shifting is gross-form, not fine-detail. She can approximate, not perfectly impersonate. Voice is not included in the package. She has never passed as a specific named individual under sustained scrutiny.

**Stormranger as exception that proves the rule.** The Kree nanotech suit (Ahmed run, 2019) gave her, briefly, projected ranged capacity, flight, and offensive armament. She rejected it. The fact that she **destroyed her own access to ranged power** rather than incorporate it is itself a tell (§6.6).

### 6.3 Skill Stack (Non-Powered Capacities)

A total-surveillance file should not collapse the subject into her metahuman profile. Her non-powered capacities are substantial and operationally relevant.

- **High verbal-narrative intelligence.** Above-grade reading; fluent in genre conventions across superhero fiction, anime, fantasy, gaming. Constructs and consumes story rapidly. Operationally she **war-games via narrative template** — "what would a hero do here" is not a slogan but a working heuristic she can run on the fly.
- **Composition and prose.** Fan-fiction practice from early adolescence produced unusual fluency for her age; she writes well, fast, and habitually. Surveillance trace: extensive online posting history under pseudonyms (Sloth Baby Productions et al.), continuous since early teens.
- **Languages.** Conversational Urdu (heritage, household-level fluency, not academic); ritual Arabic (Qur'anic, not conversational); English (native). Some Punjabi exposure via extended family. Tactical relevance: she can navigate Karachi without interpreter, which is why Karachi was a viable flight destination post-*CWII*.
- **Religious literacy.** Working knowledge of Islamic jurisprudence at lay level — sufficient to argue with her brother Aamir, to negotiate observance under operational constraint (prayer time during patrol, halal sourcing on the road), to mentor younger Muslim characters into the work.
- **STEM-adjacent literacy via Bruno.** Not a scientist herself, but long-term exposure to Bruno Carrelli's engineering/chemistry work has given her unusual fluency in *what is possible* with applied science. She knows what to ask for. This matters because her power has no built-in tech interface; her gadget access is socially mediated.
- **Tactical and team-leadership skills, acquired.** None at origin; substantial by Champions tenure. She can organize a multi-power team, allocate roles to unfamiliar metas, run a rescue, manage media. She did not seek this skill set; it accrued because she kept being the person who would.
- **Improvised social engineering.** She talks her way past adults constantly — teachers, cops, parents of friends, hostile bureaucracy. Disarming-via-earnestness is a learned move, not native shyness.
- **Combat.** Self-taught, learned on the job, with intermittent Avengers-side coaching. She is **not a trained martial artist** and the canon is consistent about this: her fighting style is improvisational, power-dependent, and would be unimpressive stripped of polymorphism. This is a meaningful vulnerability against opponents who can neutralize her shifting.
- **Civilian skills.** Sewing (the costume); cooking (limited, family-mediated); driving (acquired late, reluctantly); social-media navigation (native).

### 6.4 Growth Curve Across the Canon

**Phase 1 — Discovery (Wilson #1–11, 2014).** Power is unstable, identity is unstable, the two co-vary. She holds Carol's form involuntarily, reverts under stress, cannot calibrate scale (the early Giant Fist is consistently too big or too small), and treats every fight as discovery. Healing is fast but uncontrolled. Operational radius: Jersey City, on foot or by bus.

**Phase 2 — Consolidation (Wilson #12 through pre-*CWII*).** She has settled on her own face as default. She elongates with precision; embiggens limbs reliably; uses micro-scale rarely but competently. Sleep deprivation begins to register as a constraint. She acquires team experience (Avengers, briefly) and the first sense of her own ceiling.

**Phase 3 — Moral crisis and tactical caution (*CWII* through Karachi arc).** Power use becomes guilt-coded after Bruno's hand. She fights more conservatively, holds back, second-guesses the giant strike. Operational tempo drops. The dissociation period in Karachi is the **only sustained period in her career of complete power-disuse**, and her body tolerates it without apparent atrophy — suggesting the substrate is durable, the inhibition was psychological.

**Phase 4 — Champions and reform leadership (Waid run).** She returns to the work with a redesigned ethic: smaller-scale interventions, consent-based teamwork, refusal of the savior posture. Power use is more economical and more lethal-adjacent — she takes hits she would once have dodged because she trusts her healing more, and she has internalized her morph-recovery cycle.

**Phase 5 — Stormranger and externalization (Ahmed).** She experiments, briefly and disastrously, with augmentation. The lesson she takes is that **her power must remain volitional**; any system that acts on her impulses without her consent is to be destroyed regardless of its tactical utility. This is the most important doctrinal moment in her power-history.

**Phase 6 — *Outlawed*, the law in her name, and the price of overextension.** She is broken — not by an opponent she could not match, but by leading underage operators into a fight that exceeded their collective ceiling. The takeaway in her practice afterward is a quieter, more lateral use of power: fewer giant strikes, more elongation-as-rescue, more shielding-of-others.

**Phase 7 — Death and resurrection (ASM #26 / *Fallen Friend* / X-Men line).** Killed by an Orchis assassin via impalement; resurrected through Krakoan / mutant protocols with somatic continuity. Post-resurrection power is unchanged in mechanism but **carries a new psychological loading**: she now knows experientially that her body can fail terminally, and that the polymorphic reset is not infinite. Her use becomes slightly more conservative, her humor about her own invulnerability slightly more pointed, the deflection more pronounced. The mutant reframing also brings access to Krakoan medical and resurrection infrastructure — a meta-power her predecessors lacked.

### 6.5 Signature Applications

Across the canon, certain uses recur with enough frequency to constitute a **personal style**.

- **The Giant Fist / Giant Hand-as-Shield.** Her most-imaged move. Offensive when needed, but more often used as **shield over a civilian** — the giant palm interposed between threat and bystander. The defensive frame is statistically dominant over the offensive in her output.
- **The Long Arm Catch.** Elongation across a chasm or street to catch a falling person or seize an object before harm. This is the **single most frequent power application** in her career and the truest expression of her operational identity: *reaching further than seems possible to keep someone from hitting the ground*.
- **The Vaulting Leap.** Combined embiggened leg + elongation to traverse Jersey skyline at speed, in absence of flight. Inefficient at distance, characteristic at close-to-mid range.
- **The Cradle.** A two-handed giant cup-formation used to gather multiple civilians at once — fire evacuations, building collapses, transit accidents. Distinctly hers; few other heroes have the mass-mediated form factor for it.
- **The Body-Bridge.** Elongating her own torso into a span across a gap to evacuate civilians across her body. Self-as-infrastructure. Among the more telling moves: she literally **becomes the road** people walk on to safety.
- **Selective Embiggening for intimidation.** Standing tall over an opponent (often a domestic abuser, a school bully, an institutional bureaucrat she has cornered) without striking. The threat is the scale.
- **Micro-infiltration.** Rare. Used when no other option exists. She resists it — disappearing into invisibility runs against the deep grain of the wound her powers are organized around.
- **The Absorbing Hit.** Tanking a strike that would kill a civilian by interposing an embiggened body part, accepting the reversion-to-baseline injury, healing through the morph cycle. The Champions years feature this with increasing frequency.

### 6.6 Symptom-as-Signature: The Power Read

Every metahuman's power, in this dossier's framework, is also a **somatic statement** about the psyche carrying it. Subject's case is unusually legible.

**Polymorphism = the adolescent immigrant predicament made flesh.** The girl whose foundational wound is bicultural invisibility — *seen but not known, visible as exotic and invisible as person* — manifests powers whose entire register is the negotiation of how-much-space-to-take-up and what-shape-to-be-in. The first involuntary act of her power was to **become someone else, specifically the whiter, taller, blonder ideal**. Her central origin work was learning to revert to and choose her own face. Every subsequent use of polymorphism re-traverses this circuit at low voltage. The power is not metaphor for the wound; **it is the wound made operable.**

**Embiggening as occupation of space.** A girl whose social context demanded smallness — model-minority quiet, good-Muslim-girl deferential, immigrant-daughter accommodating — got a power whose primary expression is *taking up more room than anyone expects*. The embiggened fist is, in addition to a weapon, an **assertion**. She is most-herself when she is largest, which is the inverse of the social compression she grew up inside.

**Shrinking-aversion as anti-disappearance.** She *can* shrink, capably. She rarely does. The symbolic cost of voluntary invisibility is higher than its tactical benefit. The girl whose wound is being unseen will not, except under duress, choose to disappear.

**Healing-by-reversion as identity affirmation.** Her body's repair mechanism is to **return to its own true shape**. The damage from being someone else is undone by being herself again. There is no cleaner literalization of the integrative work her psyche is doing. The cost of overextension is forced authenticity — which is also the cure.

**No projection / no ranged power as values-encoding.** She cannot hurt at a distance. She must be *present* to act. Her power forbids the predictive-policing, drone-strike, action-at-a-distance modality that *Civil War II* taught her to hate. The body-only constraint **enforces consent and proximity** as preconditions of her intervention. She cannot become Carol-during-*CWII* even if she wanted to, because her power is structurally incapable of acting on a target she has not chosen to meet.

**Mimicry-aversion as resolved trauma.** She has shape-shifting in her toolkit and uses it least. Every mimicry act is a return to the origin wound — to the moment she became Carol because she wished to be other-than-herself. Her practical refusal of this capacity is the most consistent piece of self-care in her behavioral file.

**Stormranger destruction as doctrinal commitment.** The suit offered everything her power lacks — flight, projection, augmented combat — at the price of acting on her without her consent. She destroyed it. **She will not be augmented by anything that bypasses her will, even at the cost of remaining tactically limited.** This is the operational rule of her career and the single best predictor of her behavior under future offers of power.

**The Cradle, the Long Arm Catch, the Body-Bridge as composite tell.** Her three most-characteristic moves are all **infrastructure of rescue**, not weapons. The girl whose home community had to build its own networks of mutual aid against a hostile macro-environment grew up to have a body that can literally *be* the network. She does not deploy force; she deploys **reach, capacity, and surface**. This is, in the deepest sense, what she does for a living.

**The hunger spike as honest accounting.** Her body charges for its services in calories and demands payment immediately. Unlike heroes whose power is free at point of use, she cannot pretend her work is costless. The post-fight gyro is a daily reminder that **everything she does has a body-debt attached**, which keeps her honest about her own limits in a way that more exotic powers do not enforce on their bearers.

### 6.7 Operational Profile (Tactical Summary)

- **Optimal engagement envelope:** dense urban terrain at close-to-mid range, with civilians present requiring protection. She is built for crowded streets, building collapses, transit incidents, hostage scenarios, mass evacuations. Jersey City is not incidental to her effectiveness; it is **the terrain her power was made for**.
- **Suboptimal engagement envelope:** open terrain against ranged or flying opponents; sustained engagements without rest/food; opponents who can neutralize her concentration (telepaths, sensory overload, sleep-effecting); operations requiring sustained impersonation.
- **Force multipliers:** Bruno's engineering support; Champions-style team integration; the Jersey neighbor network (civilian intelligence, safehousing, mutual aid); Krakoan medical infrastructure (post-resurrection).
- **Force dividers:** moral injury (drops her combat effectiveness measurably — *CWII* and post-*Outlawed* both show this); guilt-loading (she pulls strikes when she should not); authority figures she has pre-loaded with hero-template (she defers when she should override).
- **Failure mode:** over-extension to the point of body-failure, in service of someone she will not abandon. This has happened repeatedly and will happen again. It is the single most reliable prediction in her file.
- **Recovery mode:** community + re-articulation of principles + return to the smallest possible scale of meaningful action. She does not reset by withdrawing into self; she resets by **returning to a porch in Jersey and the people on it**.

The body she has is the body the wound demanded. The fact that she has, across a decade of canon, made it into an instrument of *rescue* rather than of *passing* is the central achievement of her career and the truest single index of who she is.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

## SUBJECT: KAMALA KHAN / MS. MARVEL

---

## 6.0 Framing

The subject is, by tradecraft standards, a *self-taught amateur* who has been operating continuously since age sixteen and has accumulated, through sheer repetition and a tight feedback loop with a small civilian support cell, a body of practical method that exceeds what her formal training (none) would predict. She has no military, intelligence, law-enforcement, or martial-arts background. Her operational education is the cumulative average of: (a) Avengers fan-fiction and consumed superhero media, (b) on-the-job pattern-matching, (c) tutelage by Carol Danvers (limited, mixed, and now psychologically compromised), (d) collaboration with peer operators in the Champions, and (e) the engineering output of one civilian asset (Bruno Carrelli) whose contribution to her survivability cannot be overstated.

She is a *neighborhood operator* who has been forced upward into team-, city-, and event-scale operations against her natural altitude. She performs best at the block level. She is reliably competent at the city level. She is structurally over-extended at any larger scale, and her worst decisions are clustered there.

---

## 6.1 Decision-Making Process

### 6.1.1 The four-beat loop

Across hundreds of documented engagements, the subject's decision cycle resolves to a consistent four-beat structure:

1. **Narrative framing.** Within the first one to three seconds of a developing situation she silently labels it via a story template — "this is the part where," "this is like when," "okay, what would [X] do." This is verbalized aloud roughly 30–40% of the time as muttered self-talk, and is observable on lip-read even when sub-vocalized. Frame templates are drawn from a finite library: Avengers canon, X-Men canon (post-resurrection, increasingly), her own prior engagements, and — diagnostically — Bollywood and YA-novel beats when the situation is interpersonal.
2. **Moral check.** Before tactical assessment, she runs a consent/dignity filter. "Is anyone here who didn't sign up for this." "Are civilians out." "Is the person I'm about to hit a person." This check is *non-negotiable* and is the single most reliable predictor of her next action. Operations that violate it (predictive detentions during *Civil War II*) produce delayed but inevitable defection.
3. **Tactical improvisation.** Only after 1 and 2 does she actually plan, and the plan is almost always improvisational — a single primary action with one fallback, rarely more. She does not pre-stage contingency trees. She trusts her morph to absorb the consequences of a bad first move.
4. **Post-action narration.** During and after, she narrates — to herself, to teammates, to civilians, to opponents. This is partly nervous habit, partly community-building reflex, and partly a debrief-in-real-time that allows her to update the template library mid-engagement.

### 6.1.2 Failure modes of the loop

- **Template lock-in.** Once she has labeled a situation, she is slow to re-label. Adversaries who present as one archetype and pivot mid-engagement get extra free seconds. (Doc.X exploited this; the Inventor exploited this initially.)
- **Authority deference at the moral-check stage.** When a pre-loaded hero figure is the one ordering the morally-suspect action, her filter mis-fires and waves it through. *Civil War II* is the canonical example; the wound has tightened the filter, but the vulnerability is structural, not extinct.
- **Single-fallback fragility.** With only one fallback queued, second-order failures cascade. She compensates with raw morphic durability, which is why she takes so many hits.

### 6.1.3 What she will *not* do

A short list, exhaustively reliable across canon:

- She will not kill. Not as a tactical choice; as an identity constraint.
- She will not deceive a civilian who has asked her a sincere question, with the exception of identity-protection.
- She will not break a promise made to family, even at significant operational cost — she will reschedule a patrol around iftar, around her brother's nikah, around her mother's expectations of dinner attendance.
- She will not act on intelligence she considers ethically tainted (precog, coerced confession, surveillance she'd refuse to endorse publicly).
- She will not abandon a teammate in the field, even when tactically correct to do so. This is exploitable and has been exploited.

---

## 6.2 Methods & Combat Tradecraft

### 6.2.1 Morphic toolkit, operationally categorized

Her powers, viewed as a *toolset* rather than a phenomenon:

- **Embiggening (limb scale).** Primary combat verb. Used for: striking at range without closing, blocking ordnance, catching falling civilians (the single most-used application across the canon), forming bridges, prying doors, lifting vehicles. Cost: proportional fatigue; cognitive load increases with mass.
- **Embiggening (full body).** Reserved for crowd-scale protection (shielding bystanders, bracing collapsing structures) and rare brawler engagements. She visibly dislikes the full-body giant form — it draws photography, makes her hyper-visible (the original wound), and exhausts her fastest.
- **Elongation.** Movement, retrieval, non-lethal restraint. Her preferred restraint method is to coil around a limb or torso, not to strike. This is a signature.
- **Shrinking.** Reconnaissance, escape, ingress through HVAC and small apertures, hiding inside structures or even garments. Under-used relative to its potential; she dislikes the vulnerability of being small.
- **Limited shape mimicry.** Used sparingly and badly. She is a poor impersonator — faces come out uncanny, voices do not match. She avoids ops requiring this.
- **Healing via reversion.** This is not deployed; it is *forced*. Sufficient injury collapses any held morph back to baseline. Operationally this means she cannot maintain disguise under fire, cannot remain embiggened when concussed, and her "true form" is the recovery state — which has obvious identity-exposure implications addressed below (§6.5).

### 6.2.2 Engagement geometry

She fights, almost without exception, from a **defensive forward** posture: between the threat and the civilians, body angled to catch incoming fire on her own mass, dominant hand (right) usually the one she embiggens first. She prefers to *interpose* rather than *intercept*. The geometric tell: in a crowded scene, find the civilian most exposed and draw a line to the nearest cover — she will be standing on that line.

She does not flank. She does not pincer. She does not bait. She *stands in front of things*. Adversaries who understand this can route around her by threatening multiple civilian vectors simultaneously, which forces her into the size-up failure mode where she tries to be in two places by elongating and ends up effective in neither.

### 6.2.3 Force calibration

Her strike force is heavily downscaled relative to her capacity. She pulls punches as a near-reflex; documented instances of full-power strikes are rare and almost all post-*Civil War II*, on inorganic targets (Stormranger, robotics, structural). Against organics she defaults to: grapple, restrain, displace, talk. Verbal de-escalation is part of the combat sequence, not separate from it — she will be talking the entire engagement.

### 6.2.4 The talking

The narration is operationally significant in three ways:

- **De-escalation.** Many opponents stand down or hesitate when addressed as people. She knows this and uses it deliberately.
- **Crowd management.** She issues civilian instructions inside the patter ("sir, back up; ma'am, the door's that way; kid, eyes on me, walk").
- **Team coordination.** In Champions ops she narrates to the team without using comms protocol, which is sloppy but functional within a small trust-dense unit.

The cost is broadcast: anyone listening knows her plan as she forms it. This has cost her surprise on multiple occasions.

---

## 6.3 Tradecraft (Non-Combat)

### 6.3.1 Identity protection

Her cover is *poor by professional standards and adequate by neighborhood ones*. Specifically:

- **Costume.** Hand-sewn from a repurposed dishdasha and modified across multiple iterations; constructed for modesty (long sleeves, leggings, scarf, tunic-length top) and for the symbolic continuity of her name with Carol Danvers. The lightning bolt is large, contrasting, and visible at distance — operationally a *liability* (high-recognition silhouette) deliberately accepted for *identity* reasons (visible declaration of presence; the opposite of the white-blonde morph she rejected).
- **Mask.** Domino, partial. Covers eyes only. Functionally useless against anyone who has met her unmasked or possesses facial-recognition above consumer grade. Operates within the broader superhero convention that the mask is *socially* respected by adversaries with civilian-life codes; it offers no protection against professional intelligence opposition.
- **Hair.** Visible, dark, distinctive. No attempt at concealment.
- **Voice.** Unaltered. Her speech pattern is highly characteristic (see §6.7) and identifying.
- **Body morphology.** Variable under power use, but reverts under injury — meaning a sufficiently aggressive opponent can force her back to baseline civilian dimensions mid-fight, which is a *catastrophic* identity-protection failure she has survived only because the opponents present at such moments have not been the ones who would weaponize the intelligence.

People who know her identity: family (Yusuf, Muneeba, Aamir, Tyesha — late discovery, after Aamir's marriage); Bruno Carrelli (since day one, operationally indispensable); Nakia Bahadir; Mike (Bruno's girlfriend); Zoe Zimmer (later); Carol Danvers; Tony Stark and most senior Avengers; her Champions teammates; subsequently key X-Men. The set is large and growing — by professional standards her identity is *not secret*, only locally discreet.

### 6.3.2 Communications

- Personal mobile phone, civilian carrier, no documented OPSEC hardening beyond standard adolescent settings. She texts on patrol, has been observed taking selfies in costume, runs at least one social-adjacent account in costume persona.
- Champions comms: standard team channel, basic encryption (Stark-grade or equivalent through team infrastructure); her personal discipline on the channel is poor — she narrates, jokes, breaks radio silence.
- Family comms: she answers her mother's calls *during operations*. This is a non-negotiable behavioral fact and an exploitable one — her phone is on, locatable, and she will pick up.

### 6.3.3 Surveillance and counter-surveillance

She does almost none. She is observed but does not observe. Recon is conducted by walking up to a thing and looking at it, often in costume. She does not pre-walk routes, does not establish patterns of an adversary before engaging, does not run sustained collection. When she does collect, it is via Bruno (signals, technical) or via her network of neighborhood informants (humint — see §6.4.3).

Counter-surveillance is similarly weak: she does not check for tails, does not vary routes between civilian and operational life, and has been followed home repeatedly in canon.

### 6.3.4 Information discipline

Loose in person, surprisingly tight in writing. She does not journal operational details; her notebooks are full of sketches and fan-style narrative annotations. She does not maintain target dossiers. Most of her intelligence lives in her head and in Bruno's lab notebooks.

She is, however, *quick* to confide in trusted persons, and her trust threshold is low and warm. Pressure on those persons is the standard route to operational information about her.

---

## 6.4 Resources & Infrastructure

### 6.4.1 Financial

Essentially nil personal funding. She is a teenager / young woman with no employment income beyond episodic part-time work; her family is comfortable lower-middle to middle-class (father in banking-adjacent finance; mother homemaker); she has no superhero stipend in any sustained form. Avengers-affiliated periods provided incidental access to facilities and equipment but not to liquid capital under her control. Champions affiliation provided team infrastructure (transport, base access) similarly without personal funding.

Operational consequence: her tradecraft is *cheap by necessity*. Hand-stitched costume; repaired rather than replaced; equipment is whatever Bruno fabricates from accessible materials; transport is public (PATH, NJ Transit, bus) or by power (elongation, sized leaps) or by piggybacking on team resources.

She does not maintain safe houses. She does not maintain caches. She does not maintain go-bags in any disciplined sense. She has no false identity documents. She has no offshore anything.

### 6.4.2 Physical infrastructure

- **Home (Khan residence, Jersey City).** Primary base by default. Her bedroom is operational HQ — costume storage (poorly concealed; her mother has found it), notebooks, devices. This is an OPSEC nightmare and a deeply human fact.
- **Circle Q convenience store.** Civilian node; Bruno-adjacent in the earliest period; neighborhood gravity well.
- **Bruno's lab / family gyro shop / later Coles Academic High School lab.** Real operational base. Equipment fabrication, comms, medical patching, debrief space. Bruno post-Wakanda has degraded this node; her infrastructure has thinned proportionally.
- **Champions facilities.** Mobile (the airship) and stationary, team-shared. She uses these but does not control them.
- **Avengers facilities.** Access has waxed and waned with affiliation and political climate (post–*Kamala's Law*: zero).
- **Masjid and broader Jersey City Muslim community.** Not "operational infrastructure" in any tradecraft sense, but functionally one of her most reliable shelters, information networks, and crowd-management resources.

### 6.4.3 Human network

The single largest asset she controls. Categorized:

- **Inner cell (operationally cleared, identity-aware, mission-capable):** Bruno Carrelli (engineering, medical-adjacent, emotional regulation, identity-protection); Nakia Bahadir (civilian intelligence, community standing, moral counsel); Aamir (post-disclosure, family-side cover and protection); Mike (peripheral but cleared).
- **Trusted operators (peer heroes):** Champions roster (Miles Morales, Sam Alexander, et al.); Carol Danvers (compromised relationship, asset-status retained but with caveats); selected X-Men post-resurrection.
- **Family (identity-aware, non-operational, protected):** Yusuf, Muneeba, Tyesha. They are not assets; they are protected. The distinction is doctrinal for her.
- **Neighborhood humint.** Functionally enormous: Jersey City residents who recognize her, like her, and pass her information; shopkeepers, masjid attendees, school contacts, the kids who watch from windows. This network has saved her more often than any technology has, and is the operational embodiment of her core ethic — protect the unseen, the unseen protect you.

### 6.4.4 Equipment

Minimal. Costume; phone; whatever Bruno currently has working; intermittent Avengers/Champions/X-issued gear. No personal weapons, ever. No body armor beyond the costume (which functions as cover, not armor). No surveillance kit. No medical kit on her person consistently. She heals by reversion; she patches via Bruno or via masjid contacts or via emergency room visits as civilian Kamala Khan, which she has done.

---

## 6.5 Patterns of Action

### 6.5.1 Tempo

She operates on a **bimodal** schedule: school/family obligations daytime, patrols and engagements night. This produces chronic sleep deprivation (see §2 medical) and a predictable window of degraded performance in late-night ops (post 0200 local) where her judgment errors cluster.

She does not run sustained operations across days without a return-to-base for family contact. Maximum continuous time away from Jersey City prior to *Civil War II* was hours, not days. The Karachi flight was anomalous and explicitly dissociative.

### 6.5.2 Engagement frequency and selection

She does not select engagements by threat level; she selects by *proximity and visibility*. The mugging on her block always takes priority over the alien incursion two states over, structurally. This is sometimes a strength (consistent neighborhood presence, low false-negative rate on local threats) and sometimes a weakness (Champions and Avengers calls take her out of her zone, where she is less effective and more anxious).

### 6.5.3 Escalation behavior

Mapped at §5 in the shared assessment and confirmed operationally: humor → over-extension → moral-injury withdrawal → reconstitution. Operationally this means an adversary trying to *break* her achieves nothing through physical escalation (she absorbs it and over-functions in response) and achieves a great deal through *moral compromise of an institution she trusts* — which is a far harder vector to mount but a far more effective one when mounted.

### 6.5.4 Recovery behavior

After a difficult engagement: she goes home. Specifically, she goes to her bedroom, sometimes via the window, sometimes via the front door with a cover story; she eats something her mother left out; she sleeps in the costume more often than she should. After a *traumatic* engagement she becomes uncharacteristically quiet, deflects via humor when pressed, and seeks Bruno or Nakia rather than family — protecting the family from the cost of knowing.

---

## 6.6 Signature Operational Tells

For analytic recognition; the small things that consistently mark her work.

### 6.6.1 Physical / kinetic tells

- **The right hand goes first.** Embiggening initiates in the right hand approximately 80%+ of observed engagements.
- **Coil-restraint over strike-restraint.** When restraining a person she elongates around rather than striking down. Strangulation-pattern restraint is *absent* — coils are always limb or torso, never neck. This is a doctrinal choice readable as a tell.
- **Catch posture.** When falling civilians are in play she goes into a wide low brace with both arms extended and enlarged — repeatable, recognizable silhouette.
- **Reversion blink.** When forced back to baseline by injury she shudders briefly and her eyes close for roughly half a second before she reorients. Adversaries who recognize this have a half-second window.
- **Off-hand to chest at reversion.** She touches her own sternum with the left hand when reverting, a self-locating gesture. Unconscious. Consistent.

### 6.6.2 Verbal tells

- **"Okay, okay, okay"** as a self-regulation phrase preceding action. Three-beat. Frequently audible.
- **Pop-culture reference under stress.** The more stressed she is, the more specific and obscure the reference becomes. Light stress: Avengers. Moderate: X-Men. Severe: deep-cut fandom her opponent cannot possibly recognize. This is involuntary and diagnostic.
- **"Sorry"** mid-engagement, directed at opponents she is physically defeating. Habitual. Not strategic.
- **Code-switch to Urdu** in moments of high emotion (especially family-adjacent threats and prayer). Brief, often a single phrase.
- **Address civilians by relational kin terms** when calming them — "auntie," "uncle," "bhai" — across ethnic lines, occasionally to comic effect.

### 6.6.3 Operational tells

- **She arrives from the wrong direction.** She does not approach via obvious vectors because she has not planned her approach; she came from wherever she was, which is usually home, school, or the gyro shop. Predicting her arrival vector is harder than it should be precisely because it is unplanned.
- **She will pick up her phone.** Mid-engagement, if it is her mother, she will answer. This is reliable enough to schedule against.
- **She leaves the scene last.** Civilians out first, teammates next, her last — even when injured, even when she is the priority extraction.
- **She returns to the scene.** Within 24–72 hours she will physically revisit a location where something significant happened, often in civilian clothes, often alone. This is a recovery ritual and a re-narration behavior; it is also a surveillance opportunity.
- **She writes about it.** Not in operational logs — in fan-fic adjacent prose, sketches, sometimes journal-form. These artifacts exist in her bedroom and in cloud accounts with consumer-grade security.
- **She thanks people.** After ops involving civilian assistance she returns, in or out of costume, to thank specific helpers by name. This is the operational expression of her core wound transmuted to ethic — the unseen will be seen, by her, deliberately.

### 6.6.4 The negative tells (things she conspicuously does *not* do)

- No kill, ever.
- No interrogation beyond conversational pressing; she does not coerce.
- No surveillance of civilians, full stop.
- No deception of allies on matters of consequence.
- No acceptance of black-budget or untransparent resourcing — she has declined offers.
- No public denigration of opponents; even villains are addressed with a baseline of grammatical personhood.

---

## 6.7 Synthesis: Operational Character

The subject operates as a *neighborhood guardian who has been repeatedly drafted into larger theaters*. Her tradecraft is the tradecraft of a person who learned the job by doing it in front of her neighbors and who has never stopped treating the neighbors as the primary stakeholders. By professional intelligence standards she is leaky, sentimental, under-resourced, over-exposed, and tactically improvisational to the point of recklessness. By the standards that matter to her — the standards by which she would want to be evaluated — she is consistent, principled, recoverable from error, and trusted by the people she protects, which is the operational asset that has kept her alive through threats that ought, by any technical accounting, to have ended her.

Her tradecraft is, in the end, *legible* — to her community, to her adversaries, to anyone watching. She has chosen legibility over concealment because illegibility is the wound she was trying to heal in the first place. The lightning bolt on the chest is not a tactical error; it is a thesis. Everything else in her operational profile is downstream of that choice.

Any future planning involving the subject should treat her as: low-cost to surveil, low-cost to predict in any single engagement, *high*-cost to deflect from her stated principles, and effectively impossible to recruit against the populations she has defined as hers.

— UATU, Section 6 of dossier continues.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE

## Subject: KAMALA KHAN

---

## 6.1 Preliminary Note on Method

What follows is a reconstruction of the subject's working metaphysics, ethics, political theory, and tactical doctrine as derived from a decade of observable behavior, dialogue, internal monologue (where rendered), and structural choices under pressure. Where the subject would not herself articulate a principle in formal language, the principle is inferred from repeated action. Where she has articulated it, the language is hers and is cited as such. The subject is, importantly, a *narrative* thinker rather than a systematic one — her code is held in the form of stories, examples, and rules-of-thumb, not propositions. Translating it into propositional form is a UATU artifact; she would recognize most of it, contest some of it, and probably apologize for the rest.

---

## 6.2 Metaphysics in Practice: What She Believes the World Is

The subject operates from a layered cosmology that is rarely surfaced and never reconciled, but which governs nearly every choice she makes.

**The world is fundamentally morally meaningful.** This is her bedrock. Events have ethical weight; suffering matters; small choices accrete into character; people are responsible for what they do. This belief survives Civil War II, survives Kamala's Law, survives her own death, and survives the mutant retcon. It is the load-bearing wall of her psyche, and it is theological in origin — she absorbed it from a household in which moral seriousness is the air. Her father's bedtime stories, her brother's prayer discipline, the moral architecture of Surah and Hadith as casually invoked by both parents — all of this preceded powers and persists through them. Even when she cannot articulate God, she behaves as though the universe is *watched*. Not surveilled; *witnessed*.

**The world is also genuinely, structurally unjust.** This is the second layer and it is in unresolved tension with the first. She has seen enough — the racism at Coles Academic High, the predictive-policing scandal, the cynicism of state actors weaponizing her name — to know that the moral order does not produce justice automatically and that institutions are systematically organized to fail certain people. She does not become a nihilist about this; she becomes an *operator* about it. The world is meaningful AND broken; therefore one works.

**History is not a script.** This is a hard-won belief, and it took Civil War II to install it. Her early reflex was to read events as if they were issues — to assume arcs would resolve, mentors would explain, villains would be defeated within an act structure. Carol Danvers' refusal to be the mentor of Kamala's fan-fic permanently disabled this. She now believes — operationally if not always emotionally — that outcomes are open, that her side does not always win, that loved people stay hurt, that her own name can be turned into a weapon by people she will never meet. She still *hopes* in narrative shapes; she no longer *plans* by them.

**People are mostly redeemable; institutions mostly are not.** This is the cleanest principle in her code, and the most consistent in her behavior. Zoe Zimmer, who began as a casual racist, becomes a friend. Bruno's grief-driven cruelty is forgiven. Even Doc.X is approached as a person before a problem. Carol is held to account but never written out. Conversely: the Avengers as a body, S.H.I.E.L.D., the state apparatus, the school administration, the carceral system, Orchis — these are treated as fundamentally untrustworthy, requiring continual vigilance and structural reform rather than reformation through good faith. The asymmetry is not naive; it is doctrinal. It is, in fact, the implicit thesis of the Champions.

**The sacred is local.** She does not theologize publicly, but her practice reveals that holiness for her resides in particulars — this gyro shop, this mosque, this stoop, this brother, this friend. Cosmic threats interest her less than they should given her job. The Jersey City skyline functions for her the way a saint's relic functions for a pilgrim: it is the *concrete* thing the abstract value lives in. She defends it disproportionately because she believes the universal is only ever accessible through the particular. This is, not coincidentally, the moral logic of a diasporic Muslim girl in a city that taught her she could be both fully here and fully somewhere else.

---

## 6.3 Theory of the Self

**Identity is plural by construction, not by injury.** She does not experience her multiplicity (Pakistani / American / Muslim / Jersey / Inhuman-now-mutant / daughter / sister / hero / nerd) as fragmentation requiring resolution. She experiences it as the normal architecture of a self. This is unusual and is the source of her durability. Adversaries who attempt to split her by appealing to one identity against another fail because she does not grant the premise that the identities are in competition.

**The self is built by what you refuse to outsource.** She believes — and this is visible in the Stormranger arc more clearly than anywhere — that what you let act for you becomes you, and what you keep in your own hands defines what you actually are. The suit acted on her aggression; therefore her aggression was no longer hers; therefore her morality was no longer hers; therefore she had to destroy the suit. This principle generalizes: she will not let lawyers act for her in moral matters, will not let mentors choose her targets, will not let teams override her conscience.

**The self is also social.** She does not believe in the self-made individual. Her identity is held in place by Yusuf, Muneeba, Aamir, Nakia, Bruno, the Khan family's mosque community, the Champions, the Jersey neighbors who have shown up for her three or four times now without being asked. She is suspicious of the heroic-isolate posture (the lone vigilante, the burdened titan) and gravitates to formations that distribute weight. She believes self-care is partially a category error: you take care of the people who take care of you and that is also taking care of yourself.

**Disguise is corrosive.** This is the lesson of her first transformation. Becoming Carol in body taught her that passing is a form of dying. She will mask for tactical purposes — the costume, the alias — but never for identity reasons. Living-as-someone-else is, for her, the only thing she categorically refuses.

---

## 6.4 Theory of Conflict

**Conflict is information.** When something is being fought over, the fight reveals what people actually value, what institutions actually protect, who is actually expendable. She reads conflicts diagnostically before she reads them tactically. This is why she is slow to enter early-stage disputes and very fast to enter once she has read the alignment.

**The fight is rarely with the person in front of you.** Her practical doctrine treats the immediate antagonist as usually a symptom or instrument. The Inventor was producing weapons but exploiting disposable kids — the *kids* were the conflict's center, not the robot. Doc.X was a hostile AI but the operative question was who got hurt in the meanwhile. Even with the Orchis assassin, her instinct (cut short by death) was to read the system behind the soldier. She fights the person in front of her with what's necessary; she does not confuse them with the actual problem.

**Violence is a last instrument and a confession.** When she has to escalate to harm, she experiences it as a failure of imagination — hers, the situation's, or both. She does not glorify combat. She does not narrate her own fights with relish. She regrets her hits. This is the inverse of how many of her colleagues operate and it is doctrinal, not squeamish. She believes that the routinization of violence in costumed work is a slow ethical drift she has watched her elders fail to resist.

**De-escalation is the default and the obligation.** Talking first is not a tactical preference, it is a moral position. She extends conversation to almost everyone — including, notably, the people who have hurt her — until conversation is demonstrably foreclosed. This makes her slower than her peers in opening exchanges and faster than them at resolution, because she has rarely cut off avenues she might later need.

**Collateral is the unit of moral accounting.** She measures her conflicts by who got hurt who did not consent to the fight. This is why Bruno's hand is a permanent wound; he was a non-combatant in her sense of him, dragged into a confrontation by her actions. This is why she opposes predictive policing reflexively: the policy turns the entire civilian population into involuntary participants in a security calculation. She will accept costs to herself nearly without limit; she rejects costs imposed on others without their knowledge.

---

## 6.5 Theory of Control and Authority

**Authority must justify itself continuously.** She does not grant standing power. Carol Danvers had her absolute deference until Carol's actions revoked it; the deference did not survive the actions. The Avengers had her membership; the moment the institutional logic of the team violated her conscience she resigned. The state issued a law in her name and she rejected the law and rejected the name-rights of the state to use her. Authority for her is a per-act renewal, not a status.

**Coercion is the master sin of institutions.** She believes the worst thing an institution can do is to force compliance against conscience, particularly under threat. This is the lens through which she reads everything from school dress codes to Kamala's Law. It is also why she founded the Champions on consent: the structural protest is "we agreed to be here, and we can leave, and our work has the dignity of being chosen."

**Surveillance is violence at a slower clock-rate.** She has not theorized this in dialogue, but her behavioral pattern is unambiguous. Predictive policing horrifies her not only because it is unjust in instance but because it *treats the future as already owned* by the watcher. She extends this intuition to corporate data collection (visible in her wariness around Bruno's Stark-funded tech), to media coverage of teen heroes, to the Inhuman/mutant registries that adjacent storylines orbit. Her ethic of consent applies to information about a person as much as to action on a person.

**Power should be held in the open and given back regularly.** She rotates leadership in the Champions, defers the title even when she is functionally in command, narrates her decisions, explains her reasoning, accepts pushback. This is not modesty; it is a theory. She believes opaque power corrupts faster than visible power and that the act of explaining oneself is part of what *makes* power legitimate.

**The state is not the same as the country, and neither is the same as the people.** She is patriotic about her neighborhood and her family and the rough idea of America as a place that could be just; she is not patriotic about any specific government. She distinguishes precisely between Jersey City, the United States, the federal apparatus, and the law-enforcement agencies that intermittently try to recruit, arrest, or weaponize her. She makes this distinction calmly and treats it as obvious.

---

## 6.6 Theory of Trust

**Trust is granular and per-domain.** She trusts Bruno absolutely in friendship and absolutely not in self-restraint regarding her. She trusts Carol in combat and not in policy. She trusts her mother with her safety and not, historically, with her secrets. She does not have a single trust register that people are placed into; she runs many parallel registers and a person's standing on one does not migrate.

**Trust is earned cheaply and lost expensively.** This is the temperamental constant. She extends initial trust freely — she is a coalition-builder by reflex — and adjusts down on evidence. But the adjustments are sticky. Once Carol broke trust at the policy level, no amount of subsequent collaboration restored that register, even as the combat register remained intact. The same will be true of any future betrayal: she does not punish, she simply does not forget where the line moved.

**Self-trust is conditional and audited.** She does not assume her own judgment is correct. The Civil War II error installed a permanent feature in her cognition: when she finds herself certain, she now checks. She seeks out Nakia, Bruno, her father, sometimes Aamir, sometimes the Champions, to triangulate before she acts on a strong moral intuition. This is not indecision; it is institutionalized humility.

**Faith is non-negotiable trust extended to what cannot be audited.** Her religious practice operates as a separate trust register that is held against her own doubts and the world's evidence. She does not justify it and does not require it to be justified. It is the place in her interior architecture where the demand for evidence is permitted to stop.

---

## 6.7 Theory of Risk

**Risk to self is cheap; risk to others is expensive.** Her risk calculus is asymmetric to a degree that approaches pathology. She will accept catastrophic personal cost — including, demonstrably, death — to avoid imposing modest cost on bystanders or loved ones. This is partly altruism, partly a residual belief that her body is the most expendable instrument in the situation because it is the one she controls most fully, and partly a failure mode (the over-functioning, the self-erasure under moral pressure) that her code permits and even encourages.

**Risk to the mission is to be hedged; risk to principle is to be refused.** She will take tactical losses to preserve the integrity of how the work is done. She will lose a fight rather than torture a captive, lose a captive rather than violate consent, lose the entire operation rather than allow predictive logic to govern it. The principles are not negotiated downward under pressure; the tactics are continuously renegotiated.

**Long horizons matter more than short ones.** This is implicit but consistent. She thinks about what kind of hero she is becoming over years, what kind of Champions roster will outlive any single mission, what kind of precedent this fight sets for the next. Her elders frequently mistake her for naive because she will accept a worse short-term outcome to protect a long-term principle; in fact this is the more sophisticated calculation and she is making it deliberately.

**Risk is to be carried, not distributed onto the unconsenting.** A version of the consent principle, again. She will not run an operation whose downside falls on people who did not choose to be in it. This rules out wide categories of tactics — terror tactics, hostage-leverage, collateral-accepting strikes — that her colleagues sometimes permit themselves.

---

## 6.8 Theory of Her Own Place

**She is not the protagonist of the universe.** This is a stabilizing belief that arrived late and is not yet fully integrated. Early Kamala did treat herself as the heroine of her own arc — the fan-fic habit of mind. Mature Kamala holds, often uncomfortably, that her story is one of many, that other people are running their own arcs with equal validity, that her death did not stop the world (the world stopped briefly, mourned, and continued), and that this is not a tragedy but a feature. The discipline of de-centering herself is ongoing and frequently fails under stress, when she reverts to over-functioning as if she were the load-bearing element of every situation.

**She is, however, *somebody's* protagonist, and that is sacred.** She is her parents' daughter, Aamir's sister, Bruno's oldest friend, Nakia's confidante, Jersey City's local hero. Within those frames her role is irreplaceable and she takes the obligation seriously. The relevant scale of her significance is intimate, not cosmic, and she works hard to keep it there.

**Heroism is a job, not an identity.** This is a doctrinal commitment, often violated in practice. She believes — and articulates when prompted — that the costume is something she does and not something she is, and that the day she cannot tell the difference is the day she has lost the work. The Stormranger episode and the Outlawed aftermath were each, in part, failures of this distinction; the suit and the law each tried to make her hero-self total, and she had to reclaim the rest of herself from each.

**She owes her community more than her community owes her.** This is asymmetric and she knows it and accepts it. The neighborhood has held her up repeatedly; she does not expect them to keep doing it; she expects to do more for them than they do for her, because she has the powers and the platform and they have lives. This is not martyrdom — she receives care, awkwardly — but it is the default direction of obligation she perceives.

**The point is not to win. The point is to leave things better and to be the kind of person it was honorable to be.** This is the closest thing she has to a single-line credo and it is reverse-engineered from her behavior across a decade. Winning is preferable but not the metric. The metric is whether the people she was responsible for are safer, the principles she stood on are still standing, and the person she was while doing the work is one she can live with afterward. By this metric Civil War II was a loss, Outlawed was a loss, her death was undecidable, the founding of the Champions was a win, and the daily work in Jersey is a continuing partial win.

---

## 6.9 Operational Code: Decision Rules in Use

Compiled from observable patterns; these are heuristics, not laws, and she breaks them under sufficient pressure.

1. **Talk first. Always. Including to the person trying to kill you, until the moment talking demonstrably costs more than it saves.**
2. **If a tactic requires treating a non-combatant as acceptable cost, the tactic is wrong. Find another.**
3. **If an authority is asking you to act against conscience, the authority has just revealed itself; act accordingly and accept the cost.**
4. **If you are certain, check. Call Nakia. Call your father. Call Bruno. Certainty is the failure mode you have already paid for once.**
5. **When in doubt, embiggen the space, not the fist. Make room for the situation to resolve before forcing it.**
6. **Never outsource a moral decision to a system, a suit, a mentor, or a law. The decision is the self; the self is not for rent.**
7. **Take the hit yourself if it is between you and a civilian. This is non-negotiable and you will pay for it eventually.**
8. **Receive help when offered, even if badly. Refusing care is its own kind of arrogance.**
9. **Forgive individuals. Distrust institutions. Re-evaluate both continuously.**
10. **Keep the work and the self separable. When you can no longer find the seam, stop and rest.**
11. **The neighborhood is the unit. Cosmic threats matter to the extent that they touch the neighborhood and the neighborhood is everywhere someone like your neighbor lives.**
12. **Tell the truth in your own voice. The disguise that costs you your face is never worth what it bought.**

---

## 6.10 Internal Contradictions and Unresolved Doctrine

The code is not internally consistent. Several tensions are unresolved and will continue to generate stress reactions and tactical errors:

- **Consent ethics vs. heroic intervention.** Her doctrine of consent and her practice of unsolicited rescue are in tension. She intervenes for people who did not ask. She justifies this by appeal to imminent harm, but the line is fuzzy and she knows it.
- **De-centering self vs. over-functioning.** She believes she is not the universe's protagonist; she acts, under stress, as though she is the load-bearing element of every room she enters. The principle and the reflex have not been reconciled.
- **Forgiveness of individuals vs. accountability.** Her capacity to forgive Bruno, Carol, Zoe — and to under-process her own resulting hurt — produces a forgiveness-without-repair pattern that the canon has not addressed and that will eventually require attention.
- **Patriotism of the neighborhood vs. cosmopolitan obligation.** She loves Jersey City disproportionately and knows she does. She has not theorized what she owes the people who are not her neighbors, beyond a vague universalism that her actual choices do not always honor.
- **Faith as non-audited trust vs. her general commitment to auditing trust.** She permits the exception and does not justify it. She is right to permit it, and the asymmetry is a real one in her interior life.

These are not failures of her code. They are the live edges of a working ethical operating system, of the kind that a person who is actually thinking rather than reciting will always have. The subject is, by the metric that matters most, a *serious* moral agent — one whose principles cost her things, whose contradictions she carries rather than denies, and whose self is built on what she has refused to outsource.

— UATU, Section 6 ends.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK

## 6.0 Preamble: Reading the Code From Behavior, Not Pronouncement

Subject professes a moral vocabulary borrowed from three sources — Quranic ethics (transmitted primarily through her father Yusuf and the Sheikh at the ICNJ mosque), Avengers-mythos heroic code (transmitted through fandom, paratext, and direct mentorship by Carol Danvers), and Jersey civic-pluralist liberalism (transmitted by environment). She quotes all three, often in the same paragraph. The enacted code, however, is narrower, more coherent, and more interesting than any of the three traditions she cites. It is reconstructed below from action, not from speech.

The methodological tell: when Subject *invokes* a rule ("with great responsibility…," Surah 5:32, "Avengers don't kill"), she is almost always either (a) instructing herself in a moment of doubt, or (b) instructing a younger or more compromised peer. When she is operating from her actual code, she does not quote anyone. She moves, and the move is legible.

## 6.1 The Operative First Principle: Consent and Visibility

The deepest layer of Subject's ethics is not "do no harm," not "protect the innocent," not "uphold the law." It is a paired axiom:

> *No person should be acted upon without their knowledge, and no person should be reduced to fewer parts than they are.*

This is derived, not professed. Evidence:

- The absolute, non-negotiable revulsion at *Civil War II*'s predictive detention. Subject does not litigate the policy on consequentialist grounds; she breaks with Carol the moment she understands that Josh is being held for a crime he has not chosen. The category violation is being *acted upon for an interior state one has not enacted*.
- The founding charter of the Champions, which she drafts in substance if not in name: no secret ops, no lethal force, no recruitment of those who cannot consent meaningfully (a position she later violates and then publicly atones for during *Outlawed*).
- Her treatment of villains: she refuses to unmask defeated opponents to the press, declines to publish identities of even her clones, and during the Doc.X arc takes pains to ensure that infected users are de-escalated rather than exposed.
- Her treatment of Zoe Zimmer: rather than punishing the casual cruelty of the opening BLT scene, she eventually *sees Zoe accurately* — as a closeted lesbian whose mockery was misdirected discomfort — and lets Zoe's coming-out happen on Zoe's own clock. She does not out, does not leverage, does not narrate Zoe to herself for years.
- The Stormranger renunciation: she destroys a weapon that acts in her name without her consent. The crime of the suit is not that it kills; it is that it kills *while she is asleep*. Agency stripped from the actor is, for her, the worst case.

The "visibility" half of the axiom is the mirror: she is constitutionally unable to leave a person *flattened*. She rehabilitates, recontextualizes, and re-narrates the people around her — Bruno from "best friend who loves me" into a full person with a Wakandan future; Aamir from "unemployed devout brother" into a partner, husband, and eventually an Inhuman in his own right; her mother from "controlling immigrant matriarch" into a woman with a coherent history of fear and love. She does this for adversaries too where she can. It is the ethical inverse of the wound done to her at the convenience store.

## 6.2 The Hard No's (Enacted, Not Just Stated)

Across roughly a decade of canon, Subject has demonstrated a small set of absolute refusals — actions she has not taken even when the in-story logic strongly invited them.

1. **She does not kill.** Not under provocation (Kaboom, Lockdown, the Inventor's mind-controlled teens), not in vengeance (post–Bruno's hand, post–her own death), not for tactical economy. The closest she has come is reflexive embiggened force, after which she is visibly nauseated. This is the most conventional of her absolutes and the least diagnostic; many heroes hold it. What is diagnostic is the *style* of the no — she does not moralize about it, she simply does not do it, and is mildly impatient with peers who treat the line as something to be reasoned about.

2. **She does not unmask, out, or expose.** Identity-revelation as a weapon is, for her, structurally identical to the wound done to her own face. She has had opportunities — Lockdown, Doc.X, multiple villain-of-the-week beats — and has consistently declined. When her own identity is exposed (the school knows, eventually the family knows, eventually a wider public knows), she absorbs the cost rather than retaliating.

3. **She does not lie to her father.** This is a striking, observable rule that she does not articulate. She lies to her mother often (about whereabouts, costume, injuries); she lies to Carol once and is devastated by it; she lies to school administration as a matter of course. To Yusuf she equivocates, omits, or stays silent — but the file does not contain a clear instance of a direct, eyes-met fabrication. When he asks her directly whether she is Ms. Marvel, she tells him. The asymmetry maps to attachment: Yusuf is her secure base, and the integrity of the base is non-negotiable to her in a way she does not extend even to other beloveds.

4. **She does not use her powers for personal advantage.** No cheating on tests via elongation, no embiggening to win arguments at home, no shape-shifting to evade consequences (the one clear exception — using a duplicate to attend Eid while patrolling — produces immediate moral collapse and a longer arc of guilt than the act warrants). Power is for the work; the work is for others.

5. **She does not coerce belief.** She is, by upbringing and temperament, the team member most likely to *be* a missionary, and she is conspicuously the team member who isn't. She does not proselytize Islam, does not proselytize heroism, does not proselytize her politics. When she persuades, she persuades by exposure to the person's own reasons, not by inserting hers. The Champions' recruitment style — invitation rather than recruitment-pitch — is her fingerprint.

6. **She does not abandon a fight she has started in someone else's name.** Even when she withdraws (Karachi, post-Stormranger, post-Outlawed), she does not withdraw from obligations she has personally undertaken. The Karachi flight is from the Avengers and from Carol, not from people who were relying on her specifically. This is a distinction she makes carefully and not always cleanly.

## 6.3 The Yeses She Has Talked Herself Into (and Their Costs)

The interesting ethical territory is not the absolutes; it is the zone where her code is under load and she has compromised. The pattern of those compromises is itself diagnostic.

- **Surveillance-by-proxy of her own neighborhood, early arc.** She accepts Bruno's tracking and tech assistance without securing the consent of those being observed — bystanders, low-level criminals, eventually her own family. She rationalizes this as "I am responsible for what I see," but the move violates her own first principle. She does not reckon with this until much later, when the same logic is used against her under Kamala's Law.

- **The Carol-aligned phase of *Civil War II*.** For the opening movement of that conflict she defers her own moral instrument to authority. She knows Ulysses's visions are doing something wrong; she lets the hero-template override the perception. This is the single largest fracture in her code on record. The injury done to Josh and the maiming of Bruno are downstream of *her own decision to outsource conscience*. She has never fully metabolized this — see §6.6.

- **Founding the Champions partly to atone, partly to lead.** She names the team's principles in opposition to what she has just lived through, which is clean. She also slides, over the run, into precisely the savior posture she critiqued in Carol — over-directing teammates, taking risks unilaterally, treating her own judgment as the team's ethical floor. She catches this in herself, sometimes; the catching is slower than the slide.

- **Operating under Kamala's Law underground.** She continues hero work while underage and illegal. She is correct that the law is unjust; she is also acting in defiance of a democratic legal instrument bearing her own name, and she does not develop a robust framework for civil disobedience to justify this. She acts on intuition that the work matters more than the rule, which is functionally the same epistemic move she condemns when authorities make it.

- **Post-resurrection acceptance of the mutant retcon.** She accepts a re-categorization of her own origin with what an observer might call ethically suspicious ease. The grace is real; it is also avoidant. She has not asked, on-page, *who decided this and on whose authority*. The first principle (consent, visibility) would normally require that interrogation. She skips it. The skip is consistent with her post-death avoidance pattern, not with her usual ethical rigor.

## 6.4 The Religious Substrate (and What It Actually Does)

Subject's Islam is operative, not decorative, and it operates differently than her public discourse suggests.

- **It supplies the lexicon.** When she needs to articulate why a thing is wrong, she reaches for Quranic formulations — most famously the "whoever saves one life" framing from Surah Al-Ma'idah, which is her go-to self-justification for entering a fight. This is genuine; it is also a *retrofit*. She would enter the fight without the verse. The verse organizes the act rather than generating it.

- **It supplies the discipline.** Daily prayer (observed irregularly under operational pressure but never abandoned as a practice), Ramadan fasting (observed even when injured and in costume — Wilson run has multiple beats of her embiggened and dizzy from low blood sugar in late Ramadan), halal observance, modesty in dress that survives into her costume design. These produce a body that is *trained* in self-regulation around impulse, which is part of why her absolutes hold.
